Gospel Hymns [modern English]

<p>Copyright &copy;2000. Used with permission.<br>Cleaveland, Inc. | 1294 Blue Hills Ave. | Bloomfield, CT 06002</p>
<p><b>PUBLISHERS' PREFACE</b></p>
<p>Gospel hymns communicate gospel truth. Paul taught that songs are useful in communicating divine truth when he wrote, "Teaching and admonishing one another in psalms and hymns and spiritual songs, singing with grace in your hearts to the Lord" (Colossians 3:16). Songs directed to God may have the added effect of teaching others. Martin Luther, whose hymns we still sing, remarked, "The gift of language combined with the gift of song was given to man that he should proclaim the Word of God through music." Singing the gospel does not substitute for preaching the gospel, but it is an effective supplement in communicating its message. Could a believer anticipate expressing his profound joy in the new song of heaven and not be interested in singing now? Could a Christian be interested in singing and yet not be concerned about the truths he sings?</p>
<p>Significantly, the compilers of "Hymns of Worship and Remembrance" (Gospel Perpetuating Fund, 1950) remarked, "People usually want to sing what they believe." The God-given ability to sing, when employed in expressing truths that satisfy the God-centered thirst of the soul, lifts our spirit to its highest objective and expresses our deepest emotions.</p>
<p>To encourage such heartfelt singing of the precious truths that we treasure and to communicate the gospel as effectively as possible, we have adapted many of the hymns in this collection. The credit after most hymns acknowledges the author whose work we have adapted and expresses our indebtedness for most of the form and content of the hymns. Hymns without a credit are original works prepared for this publication. In the credits, we have used the following abbreviations for the source of the hymns: B. H. B. ("The Believers Hymnbook," Pickering & Inglis); C. H. F., ("Choice Hymns of the Faith," Gospel Perpetuating Fund); G. H. B. ("Gospel Hymn Book," Westbank Publishers); G. H. F. ("Great Hymns of the Faith,"  Singspiration, Inc.); G. T. H. B. ("Gospel Tidings Hymn Book," Central Bible Truth Depot); H. W. & C. ("The Hymnal for Worship & Celebration," Word Music); I. G. H. B. (Irish "Gospel Hymn Book," Northern Publishing Office); M. M. ("Making Melody," Scripture Memory Fellowship International); R. S. ("Redemption Songs,” Pickering and Inglis Ltd.); S. G. H. ("Select Gospel Hymns," Northern Publishing Office); S. S. ("Salvation Songs," G. A. Ramsay); S. S. & S. ("Sacred Solos," Marshall, Morgan & Scott). The credits may also help bring to memory a tune when the first lines of a hymn are not familiar. For this reason, we have not always used exact titles when we thought another title would be more readily recognized.</p>
<p>For some time, a number of believers have felt the need for a work of this kind. This work has spanned more than three years. What has sustained the focus of this undertaking has been a love for the gospel with its lofty truths and its vital, saving, life-transforming message and also for gospel hymns, whose rich heritage we treasure and whose soul-stirring notes we have joyously employed.</p>
<p>The labors, advice, suggestions, and encouragement of many have greatly contributed to producing this work. Although they are too many to name here, we must express our indebtedness and gratitude to Jim Beattie, Bill Brescia, Al Christopherson, Tom Clark, Norman Crawford, Don Draper, Dorothy Grillo, Sandy Higgins, Phil Moore, William Oliver, David Petersen, Gayle Procopio, Doris Ramsay, Gordie Ramsay, Maria Ramsay, Bert Reilly, John Slabaugh, Tom Stickfort, Jim and Lois Thompson, Adam and Heather Thropay, and Stan Wells. In addition, we appreciate Dr. J. Lindsay Parks' preparing four hymns for inclusion in this book.</p>
<p>As noted with three of these hymns, we have contracted with their copyright owners for permission to include them in this book: "For God So Loved the World" (Brentwood-Benson Publishing, Inc.); "How Great Thou Art" (Manna Music, Inc.); and "Saved! Saved!" (Stamps-Baxter Music/BMI). We appreciate their cooperation. Two hymns by G. A. Ramsay, numbers 11 and 181, are still technically under copyright and we are grateful for permission to use them. We have contacted many others who held copyrights to most of the other hymns in this book. To the best of our ability, we have determined that these hymns are now in the public domain. A handful of hymns have been included without that determination. Due to scanty copyright information or to the fact that copyrights are sometimes sold and we have not been able to trace them, we have included hymns that we assume are in the public domain, because they appear to have been written more than 75 years ago. If we have failed to receive permission for any hymns still under copyright, we would appreciate knowing this and we request the understanding of the copyright owners until we are able to rectify this oversight. In addition, we have applied for copyrights to the original hymns or arrangements included in this book. This is a formality to protect our use of these hymns.</p>
<p>During the time since many of these hymns were written, word meanings and customs of phrasing have changed, and the style of communication has become more direct. The changes made in this collection of hymns reflect an attempt to  'translate" the truths they contain and thus to extend the usefulness, impact, and clarity of these beloved hymns. David "served his own generation by the will of God" (Acts 13:36). Our hope is that this hymnbook, in the good will of God, will serve our generation; perhaps this effort will also serve succeeding generations, if the Lord has not come.</p>
<p>From preceding generations, we have received a rich heritage of truth contained in gospel hymns. We trust that our God will be pleased to use this hymnbook to help preserve that heritage. Our humble prayer is that the gracious Spirit of God will choose to use this work in the salvation of souls.</p>
<p>On all of Johann Sebastian Bach's original works, "J. J." ("Jesu Juva" or "Jesus, help me") appears at the beginning of the work and "S. D. G." ("Soli Deo Gloria" or "To the glory of God alone") at the end. Conscious of our many limitations, we have looked to God for help as the work progressed. Now we humbly borrow the letters with which Bach concluded his works. Having compiled and adapted these hymns, we complete this publication with these initials: S. D. G.</p>
<p>E. Higgins & D. Oliver</p>

--lyrics
1
A Hand Once Bruised and Bleeding

Credit: "A Hand All Bruised and Bleeding," J. Oatman; R. S. #86

A hand once bruised and bleeding is knocking at the door;
Insisting, yet tender it has been.
It is the hand of Jesus, who often knocked before;
He's waiting to save you from your sin;

c
O don't you hear Him knocking, knocking at the door?
So loving and so tender His heart!
He gave His life to save you; He could not love you more;
How sad should this loving Friend depart!

How often through some sickness, some trouble, or some pain
This knocking resounded in your ears!
How often in your conscience the knock would come again,
So loud, it would fill your soul with fears!

c
O don't you hear Him knocking, knocking at the door?
So loving and so tender His heart!
He gave His life to save you; He could not love you more;
How sad should this loving Friend depart!

While standing by the casket of some departed friend,
In sorrow that filled your heart with pain,
What caused that mournful thinking of how your life would end?
His hand knocked in tenderness again.

c
O don't you hear Him knocking, knocking at the door?
So loving and so tender His heart!
He gave His life to save you; He could not love you more;
How sad should this loving Friend depart!

That hand recalls the story of all His shame and pain,
His nail-prints, His blood He shed for you.
No lesser price could ever salvation's gift obtain;
He loved you as no one else could do.

c
O don't you hear Him knocking, knocking at the door?
So loving and so tender His heart!
He gave His life to save you; He could not love you more;
How sad should this loving Friend depart!

Why will you keep Him knocking? Why would you choose your sin?
He offers to cleanse that sin away.
His presence brings the sunrise of joy and peace within;
Then why not receive this Friend today?

c
O don't you hear Him knocking, knocking at the door?
So loving and so tender His heart!
He gave His life to save you; He could not love you more;
How sad should this loving Friend depart!


2
Ye Must Be Born Again

"Ye must be born again" was the message of the Lord Jesus to the rabbi, Nicodemus, in John 3:The Savior told him that unless a person were born again he could not enter the kingdom of God.<br>Credit: "Ye Must Be Born Again," W. T. Sleeper; C. H. F. #37

A ruler once came to the Savior by night,
To ask Him the way of salvation and light;
The Master responded in words true and plain,
"Ye must be born again!"

c
"Ye must be born again!"
"Ye must be born again!"
I verily, verily say unto you,
"Ye must be born again!"

How vital this truth found in God's holy Word!
How solemnly spoken by Jesus the Lord!
Then let not this message to you be in vain,
"Ye must be born again!"

c
"Ye must be born again!"
"Ye must be born again!"
I verily, verily say unto you,
"Ye must be born again!"

Your dear ones in heaven you've promised to meet
Are safe now with Jesus; their joy is complete.
If you would be there, hear this solemn refrain,
"Ye must be born again!"

c
"Ye must be born again!"
"Ye must be born again!"
I verily, verily say unto you,
"Ye must be born again!"

If you hope to enter this glorious rest
And sing with the ransomed the song of the blest,
New life is required, the Scriptures explain;
"Ye must be born again!"

c
"Ye must be born again!"
"Ye must be born again!"
I verily, verily say unto you,
"Ye must be born again!"


3
He Took My Place
Alt. Tune: "Since Christ Forgave My Debt of Sin," #186
Credit: "He Took My Place," E. E. Hewitt; Tune: R. S. #298

A trembling soul, I sought the Lord;
I knew my guilt, my sins deplored.
How welcome was His Word to me,
He took my place and died for me!

c
No other hope, no other plea,
He took my place and died for me.
The willing Lamb of Calvary!
He took my place and died for me.

His work that saves is now complete;
Assured, I worship at His feet,
Since in His love so great and free,
He took my place and died for me.

c
No other hope, no other plea,
He took my place and died for me.
The willing Lamb of Calvary!
He took my place and died for me.

When sorrows cloud the light of day,
When cares or troubles come my way,
My daily strength He'll ever be,
Who took my place and died for me.

c
No other hope, no other plea,
He took my place and died for me.
The willing Lamb of Calvary!
He took my place and died for me.

No room for doubts, no room for fears,
When to my view the cross appears;
My joyful song shall ever be,
"He took my place and died for me."

c
No other hope, no other plea,
He took my place and died for me.
The willing Lamb of Calvary!
He took my place and died for me.


4
He's Hiding My Soul

The prophet Isaiah pictures a hot desert scene in which water brings relief from thirst. In addition, a large rock provides shade from the burning sun. He prophesied that our Lord Jesus would provide such refreshment and shelter to meet our spiritual needs (Isaiah 32:2).<br>Credit: "He Hideth My Soul," Fanny J. Crosby; C. H. F. #38

A wonderful Savior is Jesus, my Lord;
A wonderful Savior is He.
He's hiding my soul in the cleft of the rock
Where rivers of joy flow for me.

c
He's hiding my soul in the cleft of the rock
That shadows a dry, thirsty land;
He's sheltering me in the depths of His love;
He's holding me there in His hand.

A wonderful Savior is Jesus, my Lord;
He took all my burden away;
He's guarding my soul and I shall not be moved;
He's giving me strength day by day.

c
He's hiding my soul in the cleft of the rock
That shadows a dry, thirsty land;
He's sheltering me in the depths of His love;
He's holding me there in His hand.

Assured of all heavenly blessings in Christ
And filled with His fullness divine,
I sing with rejoicing, so grateful to God
For such a Redeemer as mine!

c
He's hiding my soul in the cleft of the rock
That shadows a dry, thirsty land;
He's sheltering me in the depths of His love;
He's holding me there in His hand.

When changed to His likeness, transported I rise
To meet Him in clouds of the sky,
His perfect salvation, His wonderful love,
I'll sing with the millions on high.

c
He's hiding my soul in the cleft of the rock
That shadows a dry, thirsty land;
He's sheltering me in the depths of His love;
He's holding me there in His hand.


5
I Come

Credit: "I Come"; C. H. F. #210

Again the blessed gospel I have heard,
That word divine and true,
For God again has spoken to my soul,
And now what shall I do?

c
I come, I come,
I come to Thee, my God; I do Thy love believe.
I do accept Thy gift of life and peace;
I do Thy Son receive.

My wayward heart has wandered far from Thee
And known no rest or home,
No present peace, no hope of joy beyond,
But now to Thee I come.

c
I come, I come,
I come to Thee, my God; I do Thy love believe.
I do accept Thy gift of life and peace;
I do Thy Son receive.

No works of mine, no merit can I bring,
No holiness within;
I only trust in Jesus Christ, Thy Son;
His blood will cleanse my sin.

c
I come, I come,
I come to Thee, my God; I do Thy love believe.
I do accept Thy gift of life and peace;
I do Thy Son receive.


6
Satisfied

The thirst of the Samaritan woman (John 4:13-15), the hunger of the prodigal son (Luke 15:17), and the sadness of the rich, young ruler (Luke 18:23) indicate the native longings of the human spirit. Man was created to find his fulfillment in a relationship with God. The Lord Jesus said, "I am come that they might have life, and that they might have it more abundantly" (John 10:10).<br>Credit: "Satisfied," C. T. Williams; G. H. F. #446

All my life long I was yearning,
Longing for some cooling spring
That I hoped would quench the burning
   Of the thirst I felt within.

c
Hallelujah! I have found Him,
Found what I so long have craved;
Jesus satisfies my longings;
Through His blood I now am saved.

Feeding on the husks around me
Till my strength was almost gone,
Still I dreamed of something better,
While my hunger lingered on.

c
Hallelujah! I have found Him,
Found what I so long have craved;
Jesus satisfies my longings;
Through His blood I now am saved.

I was poor, and sought for riches,
Hoping they would satisfy,
But the dust I gathered round me
Only mocked my bitter cry.

c
Hallelujah! I have found Him,
Found what I so long have craved;
Jesus satisfies my longings;
Through His blood I now am saved.

Well of water, ever springing,
Bread of life, so rich and free,
Untold wealth, eternal treasure,
My Redeemer is to me.

c
Hallelujah! I have found Him,
Found what I so long have craved;
Jesus satisfies my longings;
Through His blood I now am saved.


7
All Things Are Ready - Come
Tune: "We're Marching to Zion"
The parable in Matthew 22: 1-14 likens the gospel to a king's marriage feast for his son. The king sent this invitation: "All things are ready: come unto the marriage." Similarly, God invites all to freely enjoy the rich blessing of salvation He has provided.<br>Credit: "All Things Are Ready - Come"; G. H. B. #6

"All things are ready, come!"
Come to the supper spread;
Come, rich and poor; come, old and young;
Come, rich and poor; come, old and young;
Come, and be richly fed; come, and be richly fed.

c
The Father entreats you;
Kindly the Savior invites you;
The Spirit urgently calls you
To enter the banquet today.

"All things are ready, come!"
The door is open wide;
The love of God prepared the feast,
The love of God prepared the feast,
For Christ, His Son, has died; for Christ, His Son, has died.

c
The Father entreats you;
Kindly the Savior invites you;
The Spirit urgently calls you
To enter the banquet today.

"All things are ready, come!"
There is no need to wait;
The cross has fully proved His love;
The cross has fully proved His love;
Then do not hesitate; then do not hesitate.

c
The Father entreats you;
Kindly the Savior invites you;
The Spirit urgently calls you
To enter the banquet today.

"All things are ready, come!"
Should mercy's day be passed,
The night of endless gloom would come;
The night of endless gloom would come;
"Depart," He'll say at last; "Depart," He'll say at last.

c
The Father entreats you;
Kindly the Savior invites you;
The Spirit urgently calls you
To enter the banquet today.


8
Almost Persuaded

The apostle Paul's account of his own conversion and of the significance of the death and resurrection of Christ convicted King Agrippa. Confronted by the challenge of becoming a believer, he tried to evade the issue by saying, "Almost thou persuadest me to be a Christian" (Acts 26).<br>Credit: "Almost Persuaded," P. P. Bliss; C. H. F. #211

"Almost persuaded" now to believe;
"Almost persuaded" Christ to receive.
How sad if you should say, "Go, Spirit, go Thy way;
Some more convenient day I'll call for Thee"!

"Almost persuaded," come, come today!
"Almost persuaded," turn not away!					
Jesus now pleads with you; prayers rise from loved ones, too;
Time flies, what will you do?  O wanderer, come!

"Almost persuaded!" Harvest is past.
"Almost persuaded!" Doom comes at last.
"Almost" cannot avail; "almost" - all hopes will fail!
How sad the endless wail, "Almost, but lost!"


9
Amazing Grace

Credit: "Amazing Grace," J. Newton (verses 1-4); C. H. F. #40

Amazing grace! How sweet the sound
That saved a wretch like me;
I once was lost, but now am found,
Was blind, but now I see.

His grace first taught my heart to fear,
And grace my fears relieved;
How precious did that grace appear
The hour I first believed!

Through many dangers, toils, and snares
I have already come;
His grace has brought me safe thus far,
And grace will lead me home.

When we've been there ten thousand years,
Bright shining as the sun,
We've no less days to sing God's praise
Than when we'd first begun.

How strange that any hearts could spurn
Amazing, saving grace,
From heaven's open gate to turn
And endless grief embrace!

When they've been lost ten thousand years,
In darkness and despair,
They've no less years to shed their tears
Than when they entered there.


10
Amazing! The Eternal Bled
Tune: "At the Cross"
Credit: "Alas, and Did My Savior Bleed?" I. Watts; C. H. F. #33

Amazing! The Eternal bled!
Would the Immortal die?
Would He devote that sacred head
For sinners such as I?

c
At the cross, at the cross, where I first saw the light,
And the burden of my heart rolled away!
It was there by faith I received my sight,
And now I am thankful every day.

Was it for crimes that I have done
He suffered on the tree?
Amazing pity! Grace unknown
And love beyond degree!

c
At the cross, at the cross, where I first saw the light,
And the burden of my heart rolled away!
It was there by faith I received my sight,
And now I am thankful every day.

No wonder that the sun should hide
And shut its glories in,
When the incarnate Maker died
For man His creature's sin.

c
At the cross, at the cross, where I first saw the light,
And the burden of my heart rolled away!
It was there by faith I received my sight,
And now I am thankful every day.

How could I have a blushing face
While His dear cross appears?
My heart must melt in thankfulness,
My eyes dissolve to tears.

c
At the cross, at the cross, where I first saw the light,
And the burden of my heart rolled away!
It was there by faith I received my sight,
And now I am thankful every day.


11
As We Wait for Christ
Tune: "Hold the Fort"
Credit: "As We Turn Our Eyes," G. A. Ramsay; S. S. #6

As we wait for Christ from heaven,
Here's the reason why
We believe saints now are living
Who may never die:
Jesus spoke, when He was leaving,
Words so clear and plain,
"If I go away and leave you,
I will come again."

Long His Bride has waited for Him;
Dark has been the night.
Martyrs' blood has flowed in rivers;
Fierce has been the fight.
But the gospel then was sounded
And is sounding still;
Through its message God has purposed
Heaven's ranks to fill.

Dreadful day, when mercy closes
Heaven's open door!
Words of doom, what heart could bear them,
"Closed forevermore!"
All around there's ample warning
Of impending doom.
Quickly come while Mercy calls you;
Christ is coming soon!

While He tarries, do not linger;
Strive to enter in!
Now's the time to come for cleansing
From your stain of sin.
Jesus promised, "Him that cometh
I will not cast out."
Come, receive Him; come, believing;
Come, and do not doubt.


12
Behold the Lamb of God
Tune: "I Hear Thy Welcome Voice," #89
Credit: "Behold the Lamb of God"; G. H. B. #10

Behold the Lamb of God,
Who suffered for our sin.
"Look unto Me, and be ye saved";
The promise takes you in.

c
Look and you'll be saved
From your plague of sin!
Look to Christ on Calvary!
The promise takes you in.

For God so loved the world,
His only Son He gave,
That whosoever will believe
In Him new life shall have.

c
Look and you'll be saved
From your plague of sin!
Look to Christ on Calvary!
The promise takes you in.

A Lamb to slaughter led,
He loved you and He died.
His blood flowed from His hands and feet
And from His open side.

c
Look and you'll be saved
From your plague of sin!
Look to Christ on Calvary!
The promise takes you in.

He shed His precious blood
For sins of crimson stain;
Believe on Him and you'll be cleansed;
No spot will then remain.

c
Look and you'll be saved
From your plague of sin!
Look to Christ on Calvary!
The promise takes you in.


13
Beneath the Cross of Jesus

Credit: "Beneath the Cross of Jesus (verses 1 and 2), E. C. Clephane; C. H. F. #264

Beneath the cross of Jesus
I gladly take my stand,
The shadow of a mighty rock
Within a weary land,
A home within the wilderness,
A rest along life's ways
Through thirsty desert, noonday heat,
Or cold and lonely days.

Before the cross of Jesus
With grief I stand and see
The lonely thorn-crowned form of One
Who suffered there for me,
And from my contrite heart with tears
Two wonders I confess:
The wonders of His matchless love
And my unworthiness.

Beside the cross of Jesus
Stretch two eternities:
With Christ above or lost in hell -
Just these two destinies.
One thief, repenting, turned to Christ;
He heard, "You'll be with Me."
The other thief, though just as near,
Was lost eternally.

Beyond the cross of Jesus
There looms so endlessly
The darkness of an awful grave
And hell's dread misery.
But there to stop us stands the cross,
Two arms outstretched to save,
Like watchmen set to bar the way
To gloom beyond that grave.


14
Blessed Assurance

Credit: "Blessed Assurance," F. J. Crosby; C. H. F. #41

Blessed assurance, Jesus is mine;
O what a foretaste of glory divine - 
Heir of salvation, purchased by God,
Born of His Spirit, washed by the blood!

c
This is my story, this is my song,
Praising my Savior all the day long;
This is my story, this is my song,
Praising my Savior all the day long.

Blessed submission, bowing to God,
Certain of heaven through trusting His Word.
Joy in my soul comes down from above,
Knowing my Savior, knowing His love.

c
This is my story, this is my song,
Praising my Savior all the day long;
This is my story, this is my song,
Praising my Savior all the day long.

Blessed forgiveness, I am at rest;
Christ is my Savior; I'm happy and blest,
Watching and waiting, looking above,
Filled with His goodness, lost in His love.

c
This is my story, this is my song,
Praising my Savior all the day long;
This is my story, this is my song,
Praising my Savior all the day long.


15
Blessed is the Fountain

Convicted of his sin, King David longed for forgiveness and cleansing. In Psalm 51:7, he spoke these words to God, "Wash me, and I shall be whiter than snow."<br>Credit: "Blessed Be the Fountain," E. R. Latta; C. H. F. #39

Blessed is the fountain of blood
To a world of sinners depraved!
Blessed is the slain Lamb of God,
By whose stripes the sinner is saved!
Though I've wandered far from His fold,
Bringing to my heart pain and woe,
Wash me in the blood of the Lamb,
And I shall be "whiter than snow."

c
"Whiter than the snow,"
"Whiter than the snow,"
Wash me in the blood of the Lamb,
And I shall be "whiter than snow."

Thorns composed the crown that He wore
On His cross of dark, piercing pain.
Crushing were the sorrows He bore,
But His anguish was not in vain.
May I to that fountain be led,
Opened for my sins long ago;
Wash me in the blood that He shed,
And I shall be "whiter than snow."

c
"Whiter than the snow,"
"Whiter than the snow,"
Wash me in the blood of the Lamb,
And I shall be "whiter than snow."

Lord, I know I've wandered from Thee,
And my heart has gone far astray;
Crimson are my sins and I see
That my tears can't wash them away.
Savior, to that fountain for sin,
Leaning on Thy promise I go;
Wash me from my sin-stain within,
And I shall be "whiter than snow."

c
"Whiter than the snow,"
"Whiter than the snow,"
Wash me in the blood of the Lamb,
And I shall be "whiter than snow."


16
Will You Be There?
Tune: "Hallelujah! It's Done," #53 (Modified)<br>Alt. Tune: "Lord Jesus, I Love Thee" (Affection)
Credit: "Will You Be There?"; G. H. B. #172

By faith in a glorified Christ on the throne,
We give up the joys of the world to its own;
As strangers and pilgrims, we plainly declare
Our home is in heaven, but will you be there?

We're watching for Jesus, who entered within
The throne room above, when He'd paid for our sin.
A place in the glory He's gone to prepare
Where we shall be with Him, but will you be there?

We're waiting for Jesus; His promise is plain;
His word's sure and steadfast, He's coming again;
A numberless people will meet in the air
The Lord who redeemed them, but will you be there?

Our heavenly Father's rich banquet is spread;
"All things are now ready," as God's Word has said.
His house is fast filling; there's yet room to spare;
No seat will be vacant, but will you be there?


17
Look and Live

In Numbers 21:5-9, sinful Israelites were dying because of snake bites. God's cure was for the bitten Israelite simply to look at the brass serpent Moses erected on a pole. In John 3:14, Jesus used this incident to picture His own death on the cross as the only antidote for sin's effects. Eternal life can be received by looking to Him in faith.<br>Credit: "Look and Live," P. P. Bliss; C. H. F. #115

Call to every dying soul,
Look and live! Look and live!
He alone can make you whole.
Look and live!
Jesus paid sin's penalty,
Look and live! Look and live!
Suffered judgment on the tree.
Look and live!

c
Jesus was uplifted high;
To His cross now turn your eye.
Look and live! Why will you die?
Look and live!

Bitten by the curse of sin,
Look and live! Look and live!
You can find no help within.
Look and live!
Earnestly we supplicate,
Look and live! Look and live!
You will perish if you wait.
Look and live!

c
Jesus was uplifted high;
To His cross now turn your eye.
Look and live! Why will you die?
Look and live!

No one else can meet your need,
Look and live! Look and live!
Nor can works or prayers or creed.
Look and live!
Though you are by sin depraved,
Look and live! Look and live! 
Turn to Him and you'll be saved.
Look and live!

c
Jesus was uplifted high;
To His cross now turn your eye.
Look and live! Why will you die?
Look and live!

Every knee to Him will bow,
Look and live! Look and live!
Bowing then or bowing now.
Look and live!
He's the Savior, kind and just,
Look and live! Look and live!
In His Word now safely trust.
Look and live!

c
Jesus was uplifted high;
To His cross now turn your eye.
Look and live! Why will you die?
Look and live!

When I See the Blood

Exodus 12 records God's promise to "pass over" the houses of Israelites if the blood of a lamb had been applied to the door. In this way, God protected those homes so they were safe from His judgment because the lamb died.<br>Credit: "When I See the Blood," J. F. G. and E. A. H.; C. H. F. #48

Christ, my Redeemer, died on the cross,

All who receive Him need never fear,
For God will pass, will pass over you.

"When I see the blood,
When I see the blood,
When I see the blood,
I will pass, I will pass over you."

Then God will pass, will pass over you.

c
"When I see the blood,
When I see the blood,
When I see the blood,
I will pass, I will pass over you."

God now will pass, will pass over you.

When I see the blood,
I will pass, I will pass over you."

Then God will pass, will pass over you.

23
He'll Come and Tarry Not

Exactly fulfilling Old Testament prophecies, Jesus Christ came to earth to die. Before His ascension, He promised to come again. Hebrews 10:37 states that this promised return is likewise certain and will not be delayed, "He . . . will come, and will not tarry."<br>Credit: "He'll Come and Tarry Not," T. D. W. Muir; C. H. F. #408

Christ's promise to return is true;
There's hope that brightens all the gloom.
Let this our fading faith renew:
He said that He will surely come.

c
He'll come, yes, "He'll come and tarry not."
He'll come, yes, "He'll come and tarry not."
He'll come, He'll come, "He'll come and tarry not."

He made the world to which He came,
The lowly Savior, scorned by man.
Once crowned with cruel thorns in shame,
Now glorified, He'll come again.

c
He'll come, yes, "He'll come and tarry not."
He'll come, yes, "He'll come and tarry not."
He'll come, He'll come, "He'll come and tarry not."

Exalted on His Father's throne,
With grace, He welcomes sinful men;
With love, He's caring for His own,
And He will quickly come again.

c
He'll come, yes, "He'll come and tarry not."
He'll come, yes, "He'll come and tarry not."
He'll come, He'll come, "He'll come and tarry not."

What joy shall each believer know,
Though life its many sorrows brought!
This cheers our hearts while here below:
His Word is sure, He'll tarry not.

c
He'll come, yes, "He'll come and tarry not."
He'll come, yes, "He'll come and tarry not."
He'll come, He'll come, "He'll come and tarry not."

No rest for unbelievers then!
No light to brighten all the gloom!
No hope when Jesus comes again,
Just night and everlasting doom!

c
He'll come, yes, "He'll come and tarry not."
He'll come, yes, "He'll come and tarry not."
He'll come, He'll come, "He'll come and tarry not."

Now is the time - His Word is true -
To claim this Savior as your Lord.
Trust Him whose blood was shed for you
And rest on His unchanging Word.

c
He'll come, yes, "He'll come and tarry not."
He'll come, yes, "He'll come and tarry not."
He'll come, He'll come, "He'll come and tarry not."

26
Come! Hear the Gospel Sound

The Parable of the Great Supper (Luke 14:15-24) teaches that God intends to fill heaven with saved men and women. He made provision for all; no one will be turned away who accepts the gracious invitation to come while there is opportunity.<br>Credit: "Come! Hear the Gospel Sound," G. W. Frazer; C. H. F. #44

Come, hear the gospel sound, "Yet there is room!"
It tells to all around, "Yet there is room!"
Though guilty, now come near; though sinful, do not fear;
With joy the message hear, "Yet there is room!"

God's love in Christ we see; "Yet there is room!"
Greater it could not be; "Yet there is room!"
His only Son He gave; He's righteous now to save
All who on Him believe. "Yet there is room!"

All things are ready; Come! "Yet there is room!"
Christ all the work has done. "Yet there is room!"
The payment's now complete; Christ all your need can meet;
Come, claim a vacant seat; "Yet there is room!"

God's house is filling fast. "Yet there is room!"
Some soul will be the last; "Yet there is room!"
Now is salvation's day; soon it will pass away;
Grace will no longer say, "Yet there is room!"

To save a poor sinner like me.

c

c

33
Redemption Ground

The first singing recorded in the Bible is in Exodus 15; the children of Israel sang to celebrate both redemption by the blood of the Passover lamb and deliverance from Pharaoh's army.<br>Credit: "Redemption Ground," D. W. Whittle; B. H. B. #335

Come sing, my soul, and praise the Lord,
Who has redeemed you by His blood,
Delivered you from chains that bound,
And brought you to redemption ground.

c
Redemption ground, the ground of peace;
Redemption ground, the height of grace!
Here let our praise to God abound,
Who saves us on redemption ground.

Once from my God I wandered far,
Against His holy will made war,
But now my songs to God abound;
I'm standing on redemption ground.

c
Redemption ground, the ground of peace;
Redemption ground, the height of grace!
Here let our praise to God abound,
Who saves us on redemption ground.

No works of merit now I plead,
But Jesus take for all my need.
No righteousness in me is found,
No hope, but on redemption ground.

c
Redemption ground, the ground of peace;
Redemption ground, the height of grace!
Here let our praise to God abound,
Who saves us on redemption ground.

Come, weary soul, and here find rest;
Accept redemption and be blest.
The Christ, who died, by God is crowned
To pardon on redemption ground.

c
Redemption ground, the ground of peace;
Redemption ground, the height of grace!
Here let our praise to God abound,
Who saves us on redemption ground.


34
Come, Though Guilty
Tune: "He the Pearly Gates Will Open"
Credit: "Come, Ye Sinners," J. Hart; G. T. H. B. #110

Come, though guilty, lost, and sinful,
Fallen child of Adam's race!
Christ is ready now to save you;
Rich in mercy, love, and grace,
He is able, He is able,
He is willing, doubt no more.

Don't let conscience make you linger;
Don't attempt reform from sin.
Face the truth that you are helpless,
And admit your need of Him.
He will cleanse you, He will cleanse you,
He will give you peace within.

Come, though weary, heavy laden,
Lost and ruined by the Fall!
If you wait until you're better,
You will never come at all.
Not the righteous, not the righteous,
Sinners, Jesus came to call.

On the cruel tree behold Him!
Jesus for the sinful died;
Knowing all that was required
To complete His work, He cried,
"It is finished!" "It is finished!"
God by this is satisfied.

Risen, glorified, ascended,
Jesus sits on heaven's throne;
He accomplished full salvation;
Claims of merit we disown.
Only Jesus, only Jesus,
He can save, and He alone.


35
Come to the Savior!

Credit: "Come to the Savior! Come to the Savior!"; R. S. #226

Come to the Savior! Come to the Savior!
For sinners of Adam's fallen race,
He left His home above
To reveal His heart of love
And to lift us to share that home by grace.

Why do you linger? Why do you linger?
Escape for your life, do not delay.
Your time is flying fast;
Mercy's day will soon be past;
Turn to Jesus, the Savior, while you may.

There is forgiveness! There is forgiveness!
"It's finished!" at Calvary He cried.
On Him our sins were laid,
And the mighty debt was paid
On the cross by the Savior crucified.

I do believe it! I do believe it!
I'm saved through the blood of the Lamb;
My happy soul is free,
Since the Lord's forgiven me.
Hallelujah to Jesus' precious name!

37
Come unto Me

Jesus said, "Come unto Me, all ye that labor and are heavy laden, and I will give you rest" (Matthew 11:28). When He offered rest to the weary, He included forgiveness of sins, the gift of eternal life, and the enjoyment of peace with God.<br>Credit: "Come unto Me," N. Norton; C. H. F. #215

"Come unto Me"; it is the Savior's voice.
He, who alone can make your heart rejoice,
Calls to each soul with heavy cares oppressed,
"Come unto Me and I will give you rest."

c
"Come unto Me, come unto Me,
Come unto Me and I will give you rest,
I will give you rest, I will give you rest."

Weary of life with all its bitter pain,
Hear now, the Savior calls you once again;
He'll lift the burden, make the heartache cease.
"Come unto Me and I will give you peace."

c
"Come unto Me, come unto Me,
Come unto Me and I will give you rest,
I will give you rest, I will give you rest."

Guilty of sin - all hopes of heaven fade -
With conscience wakened, of your God afraid,
Turn to His cross and end the anxious strife.
"Come unto Me and I will give you life."

c
"Come unto Me, come unto Me,
Come unto Me and I will give you rest,
I will give you rest, I will give you rest."

"Life, rest, and peace" the Savior will impart,
Waters to quench the thirst within our heart,
Giving a foretaste of the joys untold
Which through eternal ages He'll unfold.

c
"Come unto Me, come unto Me,
Come unto Me and I will give you rest,
I will give you rest, I will give you rest."

Jesus Is Passing By

On His way to the Cross, Jesus passed through Jericho. Hearing this, a blind beggar grasped his last opportunity to have his sight restored and his soul saved, since the Lord would never pass that way again (Luke 18:35-43).<br>Credit: "Jesus Is Passing By," E. E. Hewitt; S. S. & S. #375

Come, weary one, He'll give you rest;
Jesus is passing by!
Come where the longing heart is blest,
And on His Word rely.

c
Passing by! Passing by!
Come to the Savior while you may!
Jesus is passing by today!
Passing by! Passing by!

Come, burdened, heavy-laden one;
Jesus is passing by!
Salvation's work is fully done;
For you He came to die.

c
Passing by! Passing by!
Come to the Savior while you may!
Jesus is passing by today!
Passing by! Passing by!

Come, hungry one, with all your need;
Jesus is passing by!
The "Bread of Life" your soul can feed
And fully satisfy.

c
Passing by! Passing by!
Come to the Savior while you may!
Jesus is passing by today!
Passing by! Passing by!

Come, contrite one, and seek His face;
Jesus is passing by!
A welcome waits you through His grace;
He'll hear your earnest cry.

c
Passing by! Passing by!
Come to the Savior while you may!
Jesus is passing by today!
Passing by! Passing by!

For God So Loved the World

Credit: "For God So Loved the World," 1st verse: F. Townsend and A. B. Smith; C. H. F. #498; Copyright 1938 Singspiration Music/ASCAP; All Rights Reserved. Used by permission of Brentwood-Benson Publishing, Inc.

For God so loved the world, He gave His only Son
To die on Calvary, from sin to set me free.
Some day He's coming back, what glory that will be!
Wonderful His love to me!

For God has sent His Son, not to condemn the world,
But that a race, depraved, through Jesus might be saved;
His hands were pierced for sins that held my soul enslaved;
Love is on those hands engraved.

Those who believe in Him shall never be condemned;
Those who believe Him not, in God's own Word we're taught,
Already are condemned and shall forever be!
Solemn is this truth for me.

On those refusing Him, the wrath of God abides,
But those who trust the Son rest on a work that's done;
They have eternal life, safe for eternity!
Faithful is His Word to me.

47
There's Cleansing Through the Blood

Twice in the Bible, cleansing from sin is compared to the unspoiled appearance of snow. King David, conscious of sins that the offerings of the Law could not cleanse, asked that God would wash him "whiter than snow" (Psalm 51:7). In Isaiah 1:18, the Lord promised that sins which were "as scarlet" and "red like crimson" would be made "white as snow."<br>Credit: "There's Power in Jesus' Blood"; G. H. B. #4

For many years my burdened heart
Sought peace, but did not know
That Jesus' precious, cleansing blood
Could wash me white as snow.

c
There's cleansing through the blood
Of Christ, the Son of God!
There's cleansing through His precious blood;
It washes white as snow.

I heard believers tell with joy
Of peace He could bestow,
For Jesus' precious, cleansing blood
Had washed them white as snow.

c
There's cleansing through the blood
Of Christ, the Son of God!
There's cleansing through His precious blood;
It washes white as snow.

I came to Christ with all my sin;
His grace had brought me low
To long for cleansing in His blood
That washes white as snow.

c
There's cleansing through the blood
Of Christ, the Son of God!
There's cleansing through His precious blood;
It washes white as snow.

He turned me to His faithful Word,
His promises to show;
I rested on its truth and knew
He'd washed me white as snow.

c
There's cleansing through the blood
Of Christ, the Son of God!
There's cleansing through His precious blood;
It washes white as snow.

I'll gladly testify to all,
While living here below,
That they should trust the Lamb whose blood
Can wash them white as snow.

c
There's cleansing through the blood
Of Christ, the Son of God!
There's cleansing through His precious blood;
It washes white as snow.

Credit: "There Is Forgiveness, God Doth Say," J. H. Burridge; C. H. F. #170

Forgiveness can be yours today,
Through the blood, through the blood,
With sin and guilt both put away,
Through the blood, through the blood,
"Made nigh" to God Himself by grace,
Made fit for such a holy place,
All stains removed - yes, every trace,
Through the blood, through the blood.

No works can cleanse your sins away,
But the blood, but the blood;
Your wealth could not the ransom pay,
But the blood, but the blood;
Our sin demands the Lamb of God,
Who shed for us His precious blood
And satisfied the throne of God.
Precious blood! Precious blood!

You may be washed as "white as snow,"
In the blood, in the blood,
And then to glory bright will go,
Through the blood, through the blood;
So come to Christ without delay,
Begin to praise the Lamb today
For washing all your sins away
In His blood, in His blood.

In heaven countless souls will be
Through the blood, through the blood;
Praising the Lamb, who on the tree
Shed His blood, shed His blood.
Caught up to meet Him in the air,
They'll praise the Lamb whose joys they share;
O happy throng! Will you be there
Through the blood, through the blood?

Once for All

The holy Law of God condemns us; Christ delivers from the Law's curse because He paid sin's penalty through His death on the cross (Galatians 3:13). To be "free from the Law" means to be no longer under its condemnation.<br>Credit: "Once for All," P. P. Bliss; R. S. #186

"Free from the Law," O joyous condition!
Jesus has died, and there is remission.
We had been ruined by Adam's Fall;
Christ has redeemed us once for all.

c
Once for all, why don't you receive it?
Once for all, why don't you believe it?
Trust in the Lord, this message recall:
Christ has redeemed us once for all.

Now we are free - there's no condemnation.
Jesus provides a perfect salvation.
"Come unto Me," how gracious the call!
Come, and He'll save you once for all.

c
Once for all, why don't you receive it?
Once for all, why don't you believe it?
Trust in the Lord, this message recall:
Christ has redeemed us once for all.

"Made sons of God" is such a high calling,
Surely His grace will keep us from falling!
Safe in His hand, we wait for His call.
Blessed salvation, once for all!

c
Once for all, why don't you receive it?
Once for all, why don't you believe it?
Trust in the Lord, this message recall:
Christ has redeemed us once for all.

Calling the Prodigal

In Luke 15:11-32, the son who recklessly spent his father's wealth, repents, and apprehensively returns to meet his father. He finds an open door, a loving welcome, and a place of honor he did not expect or deserve.<br>Credit: "Calling the Prodigal," C. H. Gabriel; R. S. #125

God is calling the prodigal; come, without delay!
Warmly He'll receive you to His gracious heart.
Though you've wandered so far from His presence, come today;
Hear His loving voice calling still.

c
Calling now for you,
Come, weary prodigal, come!
Calling now for you,
Come, weary prodigal, come!

Gently, lovingly, tenderly, still the Father pleads;
Hear, O hear Him calling, calling now for you.
Come, return while His Spirit in mercy intercedes;
Hear His loving voice calling still.

c
Calling now for you,

58
Isaiah 53
Tune: "Hallelujah! It's Done," #53 (Modified)<br>Alt. Tune: "Immortal, Invisible"
Credit: "Isaiah 53," J. L. Parks

God's Servant, the Savior, came down from above
To show us the Father, to teach us His love;
These beauties in Jesus our eyes could not see;
Despised and rejected by sinners was He.

For we are like sheep; we have all gone astray;
As sinners, we willfully chose our own way;
We needed a Lamb as the prophets foretell
To bear our transgressions and save us from hell.

Sin's debt was exacted, but we could not pay;
Yet, righteously God in His love planned a way:
The sinless One willingly died for the sin
Of those who had willfully sinned against Him!

Oppressed and afflicted by sin-hardened men,
Who mocked Him and scourged Him and smote Him again,
Almighty, defenseless (what gracious restraint!),
The Lamb stood in silence without a complaint.

For all my transgressions God wounded the Lamb;
He bruised Him, and crushed Him for all that I am.
Christ poured out His soul; He was offered for sin
And stood in the judgment where I should have been.

The Lamb is exalted; the battle is won;
God's righteous demands have been met by His Son,
Who died and was buried, then rose from the grave,
And now this same Jesus stands ready to save!

63
Are You Washed in the Blood?

In Revelation 7:14, those around the throne of God have made the death of Christ personal by faith. The graphic words of Scripture are, "they . . . washed their robes, and made them white in the blood of the Lamb." They were cleansed from sin because "The blood of Jesus Christ His Son cleanseth us from all sin" (I John 1:7).<br>Credit: "Are You Washed in the Blood?" E. A. Hoffman; C. H. F. #68

Have you trusted Jesus who can cleanse you now?
Are you washed in the blood of the Lamb?
Every other means of cleansing disavow;
Only wash in the blood of the Lamb.

c
Are you washed in the blood,
In the soul-cleansing blood of the Lamb?
Are your garments spotless? Are you "white as snow"?
Are you washed in the blood of the Lamb?

Is your hope in Jesus who was crucified?
Are you washed in the blood of the Lamb?
There's a cleansing fountain from His wounded side;
Are you washed in the blood of the Lamb?

c
Are you washed in the blood,
In the soul-cleansing blood of the Lamb?
Are your garments spotless? Are you "white as snow"?
Are you washed in the blood of the Lamb?

Soon the Lord is coming! Will your robes be white?
Are you washed in the blood of the Lamb?
You'll be saved and ready for the mansions bright
If you're washed in the blood of the Lamb.

c
Are you washed in the blood,
In the soul-cleansing blood of the Lamb?
Are your garments spotless? Are you "white as snow"?
Are you washed in the blood of the Lamb?

There's a freedom offered from sin's endless toll;
Then be washed in the blood of the Lamb!
There's a fountain flowing for the guilty soul;
Come and wash in the blood of the Lamb!

c
Are you washed in the blood,
In the soul-cleansing blood of the Lamb?
Are your garments spotless? Are you "white as snow"?
Are you washed in the blood of the Lamb?

65
Hear Now the Message

As sinners, we cannot earn salvation. God offers it freely. "The gift of God is eternal life through Jesus Christ our Lord" (Romans 6:23).<br>Credit: "Hark! Sinner, Hark; We Have Tidings So True"; G. H. B. #39

Hear now the message so faithful and true,
Telling of pardon and blessing for you;
God in His Word says that Christ on the tree
Died for guilty sinners, and salvation is free.

c
This is the message - Free! Free! Free!
Why not believe it? With God's Word agree.
Jesus, the Just One, has died on the tree,
Died for guilty sinners, and salvation is free.

God says you're guilty, but tells you, as well,
Jesus has suffered to save you from hell.
Though now condemned, justified you can be;
Christ has paid the ransom, and salvation is free.

c
This is the message - Free! Free! Free!
Why not believe it? With God's Word agree.
Jesus, the Just One, has died on the tree,
Died for guilty sinners, and salvation is free.

Earning salvation is certain to fail;
No human merit can ever avail;
Grace, grace alone, is the saved sinner's plea;
"Not of works," the Scriptures say; salvation is free.

c
This is the message - Free! Free! Free!
Why not believe it? With God's Word agree.
Jesus, the Just One, has died on the tree,
Died for guilty sinners, and salvation is free.

Some wait for feelings to tell them they're saved;
Feelings deceive, for the heart is depraved.
Trust in the Savior who died on the tree;
Hear His Word assure you: His salvation is free.

c
This is the message - Free! Free! Free!
Why not believe it? With God's Word agree.
Jesus, the Just One, has died on the tree,
Died for guilty sinners, and salvation is free.

Hear the gospel news resounding,
Christ has suffered on the tree;
Grace for all is now abounding;
God has pardon full and free;
Come to Jesus, come to Jesus,
He has died at Calvary.

See the cleansing fountain springing
From the Savior's wounded side;
To the world its blessings bringing;
Millions there have been supplied.
Do not perish, do not perish,
All may live, for Christ has died.

Flee to Calvary for refuge
And be safe in Christ today!
Soon will come the flaming deluge;
O how foolish to delay!
Do not linger, do not linger!
Come to Jesus while you may.

Mercy, cleansing, full salvation,
All in Christ alone are found.
Spread the news through every nation;
All should hear the joyful sound.
Let the heavens, let the heavens
With His endless praise resound!

69
Hell is Darkness
Tune: "Rise, My Soul, Thy God Directs Thee"<br>Alt. Tune: "Lower Lights" (combining two verses)
The Lord Jesus taught that all who die in their sins will be in hell, a literal place of torment (Luke 16:23, 24, 28). All who are there will eventually be judged by Him to determine their punishment in the lake of fire. He urged avoiding at all cost "the fire that never shall be quenched" (Mark 9:45).<br>Credit: "Hell Is Darkness"; I. G. H. B. #182

Hell is darkness, deep and awful;
Turn today, turn from your sin!
Heaven's light is bright and joyful;
To its light, come, enter in.

Hell is fire forever burning;
Turn today, yes, count the cost!
Come at once, from sin returning,
Or you'll be forever lost.

Hear the voice of Jesus pleading;
Turn today, obey His call;
See the Man of Sorrows bleeding
That He might redeem your soul.

It is finished! Christ is risen!
Turn today and trust the Lord.
Cease your working, only listen
To the message of His Word.

Hell is judgment, fully righteous;
Turn today, for mercy plead.
Turn before unerring Justice
Will the final sentence read.

God has long His grace extended;
Turn today and hear His voice.
Soon will mercy's day be ended;
This may be your final choice.


70
Himself He Cannot Save
Tune: "The Work That Saves" #219<br>Alt. Tune: "Arise, My Soul, Arise"
The accusation against Christ at Calvary was, "He saved others; Himself He cannot save" (Matthew 27:42). Though spoken in mockery, these words express invaluable truth; He could not save Himself and us. Our salvation required His death.<br>Credit: "Himself He Could Not Save," A. Midlane; G. T. H. B. #48

"Himself He cannot save,"
For sinners He must die,
Or they could never go
To live with God on high.
Yes, Christ the Son of God must bleed
That sinners might from sin be freed.

"Himself He cannot save,"
For justice must be done,
And sin's full weight must fall
On Him, the sinless One!
For nothing else could God accept
In payment of that fearful debt.

"Himself He cannot save,"
The great Redeemer stood
To pay the price of sin
In drops of precious blood.
He gave His life on Calvary;
He shed His blood to make us free.

"Himself He cannot save,"
Love's stream so deeply flowed;
He loved us and He died
To pay the debt we owed;
All God required is fully done;
Trust now in Him, God's worthy Son.

"Himself He cannot save,"
Yet risen from the grave,
He lives, the Savior-Prince,
And He alone can save;
To all the world we now proclaim
Salvation in no other name.


71
Holy, Holy, Holy

The phrase, "Holy, holy, holy," in speaking of the Lord, occurs in Isaiah 6:3 and Revelation 4:8.<br>Credit: "Holy, Holy, Holy," R. Heber; C. H. F. #17

Holy, holy, holy, Lord God Almighty;
Seraphim around Thy throne cry out in praise of Thee.
Holy, holy, holy, merciful and mighty,
God in three Persons, blessed Trinity!

Holy, holy, holy, light shrouds Thy dwelling;
Not a trace of sin abides the glory of Thy throne;
Holy, holy, holy, Thy perfection telling!
Awesome, transcendent, Thou art God alone.

Holy, holy, holy, glory enshrines Thee,
And in judgment earth shall flee Thy blazing majesty;
Only Thou art holy; there is none beside Thee,
Perfect in power, love, and purity.

Holy, holy, holy, once darkness hid Thee,
Bearing sin, enduring wrath, forsaken on the tree;
Holy, holy, holy, triumphing completely;
Blood-washed believers walk in light with Thee.


72
How Can I Tell You
Tune: "Morning Has Broken"


How can I tell you all of the changes
Since the Lord Jesus cleansed me from sin?
Dreams going nowhere, He still exchanges
For His transforming power within.

How can I tell you how much I owe Him,
Who, for my sins, was nailed to a tree?
Wrath due to me, in waves overflowed Him;
Through love undying, He died for me.

How can I tell my sacred affection
For my Redeemer, Shepherd, and Friend?
Word, He embodies every perfection;
Lord, on His love I safely depend.

How can I tell you how I'll adore Him
When I shall see my Lord as He is?
Once-wounded Lamb! I'll worship before Him,
Welcomed by Him to mansions of bliss.

How can I tell you how He will bless you?
Peace and forgiveness you will receive;
He'll set you free from sins that distress you;
Come now, the Savior's promise believe.

75
How Hopeless My Condition
Tune: "The Cloudless Day Is Nearing" (Morning Light)<br>Alt. Tune: "There's a Balm in Gilead"
In Mark 2:17, the Savior used the imagery of a physician in describing His ability to meet the spiritual need of sinners. He said, "They that are whole have no need of the physician, but they that are sick: I came not to call the righteous, but sinners to repentance."<br>Credit: "How Lost Was My Condition"; S. G. H. #30

How hopeless my condition, but Jesus made me whole!
There's only one Physician can cure the sin-sick soul.
Thank God I ever met Him, and took the cure He gave!
Then how could I forget Him, for He alone can save?

The worst of all diseases is mild compared with sin;
But this is how God sees us: sin's plague is deep within.
He gives His diagnosis: there are no human cures,
But Christ, the Scripture shows us, the remedy assures.

Sincere, and with persistence, I tried some cure to gain,
But nothing calmed my conscience or eased my spirit's pain.
No remedies availed me, regardless of the cost,
For every effort failed me and all my hopes were lost.

At last the Great Physician approached me in His grace;
He knew my lost condition and undertook my case.
He said that He was wounded to meet my soul's deep need;
That moment I depended on Him and I was freed.

The Son of Man from heaven was lifted up to die;
For all, His life was given; "It's finished," was His cry.
Then turn to this Physician, eternal life He'll give.
This is the one condition: look now to Him and live!

c
<i>CHORUS FOR ALTERNATE TUNE:</i>
Jesus Christ alone can heal your weary, sin-sick soul;
His blood alone can cleanse you and make you fully whole.


76
How Mighty a Savior
Tune: "Jehovah Tsidkenu," (Clarendon Street), #97
Credit: "How Wondrous a Savior," L. H. Farrell; C. H. F. #70

How mighty a Savior is God's blessed Son!
How great and eternal the work He has done!
God's glory's maintained by His death on the tree,
While mercy flows freely to you and to me.

How kind is the welcome His name has ensured!
How free the forgiveness His blood has procured
For all who confess Him as Savior and Lord,
Receiving His promise, believing His Word!

On Calvary see Him - what marvelous grace!
He suffered for sinners; He died in our place.
God's wrath caused His anguish on Calvary's tree;
By weakness and dying, the Victor was He.

Why will you stay distant, when God calls you near
To lovingly save you from bondage and fear?
Why carry sin's burden, when you can be blest?
And why remain weary, when Jesus gives rest?

Life's moments are passing; then do not delay!
Don't miss the salvation He offers today!
Your choice will decide where you'll endlessly dwell:
The glories of heaven; the darkness of hell.


77
How Solemn are the Words
Tune: "Blessed Be the Tie" (Dennis)<br>Alt. Tune: "Revive Thy Work" (Silchester)
The Lord Jesus told the religious leader, Nicodemus, "Except a man be born again, he cannot see the kingdom of God" (John 3:3). He emphasized that the new birth is indispensable by saying, "Ye must be born again" (verse 7).<br>Credit: "How Solemn Are the Words"; G. H. B. #47

How solemn are the words
And yet to faith how plain,
Which Jesus spoke while here on earth,
"Ye must be born again!"

"Ye must be born again!"
This is what God decreed.
Reforming is no remedy;
It's life that sinners need.

"Ye must be born again!"
And life in Christ receive.
He is the Way, the Truth, the Life.
On Christ alone believe!

"Ye must be born again!"
Or never enter heav'n;
For only saved ones can be there,
The ransomed and forgiv'n.

"Ye must be born again!"
Then look to Christ and live!
He died for sins, and by His grace
Eternal life He'll give.

My Savior

Credit: "My Savior," D. Greenwell; R. S. #395

I am not skilled to understand
The scope of all that God has planned,
But this I know, at His right hand
Is Christ, my living Savior.

I heard His Word and learned my need;
I bowed, and with His truth agreed.
"Christ died for sinners," this I read;
I claimed Him as my Savior.

He left His home; you ask me why?
He came for sinful man to die.
You count it strange? So once did I
Before I knew my Savior.

Yes, living, dying, let me bring
My strength, my comfort from this spring:
The One who lives to be my King,
Once died to be my Savior.

The apostle Paul's brilliant, educated mind grasped profound theological truths, yet he expressed the basic principle of His life so simply  in these words, "I live by the faith of the Son of God who loved me, and gave Himself for me" (Galatians 2:20).<br>Credit: "I Am So Glad," P. Jesus loves even me.

Jesus loves even me.

c
I am so glad that Jesus loves me,

I am so glad that Jesus loves me,

82
I Cannot Tell
Tune: "Londonderry Air"
Credit: "I Cannot Tell," W. Y. Fullerton; C. H. F. #172

I cannot tell why He whom angels worship
Should set His heart of love on guilty man,
Or why, as Shepherd, He should seek the wayward
And at such cost should bring them back again.
But this I know, that He was born of Mary,
That Nazareth became His lowly home;
Despised, rejected, yet He sought lost sinners,
For Christ the Lord, the Savior of the world, had come.

I cannot tell how silently He suffered
Or all the grace expressed in tender tears,
How on the cruel cross His heart was broken,
The crowning pain to all those sinless years.
But this I know, He heals the broken-hearted,
Forgives our sin, and calms our every fear,
And lifts the burden from the heavy-laden,
For Christ the Lord, the Savior of the world, is near.

I cannot tell when He'll descend from heaven
And gather home the Bride His love had sought,
Or come to earth, subduing every nation,
And rightly claim the treasure He had bought.
But this I know, His own shall share His glory,
He'll be supreme through everlasting years,
For all the earth shall bow before His splendor
When Christ the Lord, the Savior of the world, appears.

I cannot tell how great will be the worship
When, by His word, earth's many storms He'll still;
Waves of His praise shall cover all the planet;
All hearts shall know Him and obey His will.
But this I know, the skies will thrill with gladness,
The Lamb's new song shall countless voices sing;
Through endless ages rolls the mighty anthem;
For Christ the Lord, the Savior of the world, is King!

A Song of Salvation

This hymn, as originally written, provided for congregational response to its questions. These responses followed: for verse one, "This is a faithful saying, and worthy of all acceptation, that Christ Jesus came into the world to save sinners" (1 Timothy 1:15); for verse two, Isaiah 53:5; for verse three, John 14:2.<br>Credit: "A Song of Salvation," P. Phillips; S. S. & S. #1182

I have heard of the measureless love
Leading Jesus to bleak Calvary.
Can it be that He came from above
Out of love and compassion for me, for me,
Out of love and compassion for me?

c
Yes, yes, yes, for me, for me!
Yes, yes, yes, for me!
Our Lord from above, in His infinite love,
On the cross died to save you and me.

I have heard how He suffered and bled,
Bearing anguish alone on the tree;
Is it true that the Bible has said
All He suffered for sins was for me, for me,
All He suffered for sins was for me?

c
Yes, yes, yes, for me, for me!
Yes, yes, yes, for me!
Our Lord from above, in His infinite love,
On the cross died to save you and me.

I have heard of a heaven on high,
Where the children of God soon shall be;
Can I know there's a home in the sky
He made ready and furnished for me, for me,
He made ready and furnished for me?

c
Yes, yes, yes, for me, for me!
Yes, yes, yes, for me!
Our Lord from above, in His infinite love,
On the cross died to save you and me.

I have heard from the Bible, God's Word,
Of salvation so priceless and free.
It was purchased by Jesus the Lord,
And I know there's salvation for me, for me,
And I know there's salvation for me.

c
Yes, yes, yes, for me, for me!
Yes, yes, yes, for me!
Our Lord from above, in His infinite love,
On the cross died to save you and me.

I know Him in Whom I've Trusted

In II Timothy 1:12, the apostle Paul, imprisoned for his faith and facing imminent martyrdom, looked beyond death to the day of Christ's return. He expressed his confidence in the Lord's reliability with these words, "I am not ashamed: for I know whom I have believed, and am persuaded that He is able to keep that which I have committed unto Him against that day."<br>Credit: "I Know Whom I Have Believed," D. W. Whittle; C. H. F. #85

I know not why God's saving grace
To sinners He has shown,
Why I, unworthy of such love,
Was claimed to be His own.

c
But I know Him in whom I've trusted
"And am persuaded that He is able
To keep that which I've committed
Unto Him against that day."

I know not how in saving grace
God's Spirit worked within
To stir my conscience by the Word,
Convincing me of sin.

c
But I know Him in whom I've trusted
"And am persuaded that He is able
To keep that which I've committed
Unto Him against that day."

I know not all His saving grace
In agony endured,
And all His love sustained for me
Till pardon was procured.

c
But I know Him in whom I've trusted
"And am persuaded that He is able
To keep that which I've committed
Unto Him against that day."

I know not why this saving grace
He would impart to me,
By giving me His faithful Word,
His changeless guarantee.

c
But I know Him in whom I've trusted
"And am persuaded that He is able
To keep that which I've committed
Unto Him against that day."

I know not when His saving grace
Will make His plan complete
By calling me to realms above
To worship at His feet.

c
But I know Him in whom I've trusted
"And am persuaded that He is able
To keep that which I've committed
Unto Him against that day."

All His sheep are safely in His hand,
And His tender heart attends His own - O come home!

97
Jehovah Tsidkenu

The title, "Jehovah Tsidkenu," is the Hebrew transliteration of "the Lord our Righteousness" (Jeremiah 23:6). The New Testament identifies the Lord Jesus as Jehovah (John 12:38-41) and says He is His people's righteousness (I Corinthians 1:30). Belief in the deity of the Lord Jesus Christ has always distinguished orthodox Christian faith from the teaching of the cults.<br>Credit: "Jehovah Tsidkenu," R. M. M'Cheyne; R. S. #351

I once was a stranger to grace and to God;
I knew not my danger while bearing sin's load.
Though some praised the Savior who died on the tree,
Jehovah Tsidkenu meant nothing to me.

Like many when reading some heart-touching tales,
I wept for His scourging, His thorn-crown and nails,
Yet never was conscious that it was for me
Jehovah Tsidkenu was nailed to the tree.

God graciously woke me by truth from His Word;
My danger alarmed me, my conscience was stirred.
No refuge, no safety from wrath could I see;
Jehovah Tsidkenu my Savior must be.

My fears were all banished through faith in His name.
My guilty stains vanished when gladly I came
To take His salvation, life-giving and free.
Jehovah Tsidkenu is all things to me.

Should He plan my journey through death's shadowed vale,
I will not be lonely; His grace cannot fail.
Whatever the darkness, He'll still be my Guide.
Jehovah Tsidkenu, I'm safe at His side.

Jehovah Tsidkenu! He paid all the cost!
Jehovah Tsidkenu! I'll never be lost!
My Friend, my Redeemer, who poured out His blood!
My Shepherd, my Savior! My Lord and my God!


98
I Owe My All to Him
Tune: "My Hope Is in the Lord"


I owe my all to Him, my Maker and my Lord;
Both vast and small, He made it all by His own word.
Each skill, each breath to all that lives,
With kind delight, the God of might
Still freely gives.

I owe my all to Him, my God so rich in grace;
Once guilty, yet I'm kindly met by His embrace.
He brings me near, my sin forgives;
This favored place the God of grace
So freely gives.

I owe my all to Him, the Lamb, my sacrifice;
He loved, He died life to provide, His blood the price.
It is enough, for Jesus lives;
Life from above, the God of love
Now freely gives.

I owe my all to Him; His faithful Word is true;
Though undeserved, my home's reserved beyond the blue.
His Word shall earth and sky outlive;
He'll never cease, this God of peace,
To freely give.

I Saw One Hanging On a Tree
Alt. Tune: "He Died for Me" (Excell)

As near His cross I stood.

c

Who suffered at Calvary!
The Lamb who was slain is living again
To intercede for me.

I shall recall that look.
It seemed to charge me with His death,
Though not a word He spoke.

c
Christ the Lamb, the bleeding Lamb,
Who suffered at Calvary!
The Lamb who was slain is living again
To intercede for me.

And plunged me in despair.

And helped to nail Him there.

Christ the Lamb, the bleeding Lamb,
Who suffered at Calvary!
The Lamb who was slain is living again
To intercede for me.

A second look He gave, which said,
"I freely all forgive;
This blood has all your ransom paid;
I die that you may live."

c
Christ the Lamb, the bleeding Lamb,
Who suffered at Calvary!
The Lamb who was slain is living again
To intercede for me.

While Jesus' death my sin displays
In all its darkest hue,
Such is the marvel of His grace,
It seals my pardon, too.

c
Christ the Lamb, the bleeding Lamb,
Who suffered at Calvary!
The Lamb who was slain is living again
To intercede for me.<br><br>

The Savior died for me?

The Lamb who died for me.

King David used the picture of a man drowning in a stormy sea. His rescue illustrates deliverance from the enslaving, degrading, and destructive effects of sin (Psalm 18:16).<br>Credit: "Love Lifted Me," J. Rowe; C. H. F. #95

I was sinking deep in sin,
Far from the peaceful shore,
Very deeply stained within,
Sinking to rise no more,
But the Master of the sea
Heard my despairing cry,
From the waters lifted me,
Now safe am I.

c

When nothing else could help,
Love lifted me.
Love lifted me! Love lifted me!
When nothing else could help,
Love lifted me.

Heartfelt thanks to Him I'll give,
My loving worship bring,
In His blessed presence live,
Ever His praises sing.
Love so mighty and so true
Merits my soul's best songs;
Faithful, loving service, too,
To Him belongs.

c
Love lifted me! Love lifted me!
When nothing else could help,
Love lifted me.
Love lifted me! Love lifted me!
When nothing else could help,
Love lifted me.

Souls in danger, look above;
Jesus completely saves;
He will lift you by His love
Out of the angry waves.
He's the Master of the sea;
Billows His will obey.
He your Savior wants to be;
Be saved today.

c
Love lifted me! Love lifted me!
When nothing else could help,
Love lifted me.
Love lifted me! Love lifted me!
When nothing else could help,
Love lifted me.

From the curse to set me free.

With His blood He purchased me,
On the cross assured my pardon,
Paid my debt and made me free!

How, my lost estate to save,

He the ransom freely gave.

c

With His blood He purchased me,
On the cross assured my pardon,
Paid my debt and made me free!

I will praise my great Redeemer
And His triumph gladly tell,

Over sin, and death, and hell.

On the cross assured my pardon,
Paid my debt and made me free!

And His wondrous love to me;
He from death to life has brought me,
And with Him I'll ever be.

c
Sing, O sing of my Redeemer,
With His blood He purchased me,
On the cross assured my pardon,
Paid my debt and made me free!

111
If I Gained the World

The Lord Jesus asked this rhetorical question: "For what shall it profit a man, if he shall gain the whole world, and lose his own soul?" (Mark 8:36).<br>Credit: "If I Gained the World," Anna Ölander; C. H. F. #108

If I gained the world, but lost the Savior,
Were my life worth living for a day?
Could my yearning heart find rest and comfort
In the things that soon must pass away?
If I gained the world, but lost the Savior,
Would my gain be worth the lifelong strife?
Are all earthly pleasures worth comparing,
For a moment, to a Christ-filled life?

Had I wealth and love in fullest measure,
And a name revered both far and near,
Yet no hope beyond, no harbor waiting,
Where my storm-tossed vessel I could steer,
If I gained the world, but lost the Savior,
Who endured the cross and died for me,
Could then all the world afford a refuge
Where, in all my anguish, I might flee?

O what emptiness without the Savior,
Mid the sins and sorrows here below!
And eternity, how dark without Him,
Only night and tears and endless woe!
Should I somehow live without the Savior,
When I come to die, how would it be?
Could I face the valley's gloom without Him,
And, without Him, all eternity?

What abundant joy in knowing Jesus!
I can turn to Him with all my care,
Not one sin so great, but He'll forgive it,
Not one sorrow that He does not share.
If I have but Jesus, only Jesus,
Nothing else in all the world beside,
All that really counts is mine in Jesus,
And with Him I'll soon be glorified.

116
In Tenderness He Sought Me

This hymn draws together two beautiful parables of the Lord Jesus. The first is the story of a good shepherd who devotedly rescued a lost sheep (Luke 15:4-7). The second tells of the Samaritan who kindly rescued a dying victim of robbery. The Samaritan used oil and wine for medication and took the victim to a place of care (Luke 10:30-36).<br>Credit: "In Tenderness He Sought Me," W. S. Walton; C. H. F. #101

In tenderness He sought me,
Weary and sick with sin,
And on His shoulders brought me
To safety once again;
His friends together with Him sang
Until the courts of heaven rang.

c
O the love that sought me!
O the blood that bought me!
O the grace that brought me to the fold!
Wondrous grace that brought me to the fold!

He washed the bleeding sin wounds
And poured in oil and wine;
He whispered to assure me,
"I've found and made you Mine";
I never heard a sweeter voice;
It made my aching heart rejoice.

c
O the love that sought me!
O the blood that bought me!
O the grace that brought me to the fold!
Wondrous grace that brought me to the fold!

He pointed to the nail prints;
For me His blood was shed.
A mocking crown so thorny
Had pierced His sacred head.
I wonder at such love to me;
He suffered such deep agony!

c
O the love that sought me!
O the blood that bought me!
O the grace that brought me to the fold!
Wondrous grace that brought me to the fold!

I'm sitting in His presence,
The sunshine of His face,
While with adoring wonder
His blessings I retrace.
It seems as if eternal days
Will be too short to sound His praise.

c
O the love that sought me!
O the blood that bought me!
O the grace that brought me to the fold!
Wondrous grace that brought me to the fold!

So while the hours are passing,
All now is perfect rest;
I'm waiting for the morning,
The brightest and the best,
When He will call us to His side,
To be with Him, His spotless bride.

c
O the love that sought me!
O the blood that bought me!
O the grace that brought me to the fold!
Wondrous grace that brought me to the fold!


117
Depending on the Blood

Credit: "Depending on the Blood," J. Oatman; R. S. #143

In those mansions up in heaven many hope to be some day,
Yet so many are not willing to accept the living way,
But while others build on good works or opinions if they may,
Hallelujah! Hallelujah! I'm depending on the blood.

c
In the soul-cleansing blood of the Savior,
I've been washed in the crimson flood;
Though the world may say there is hope some other way,
I'm depending on the blood.

Some will tell us that God's mercy is their only hope and plea,
That a soul He would not punish throughout all eternity,
But I read that Christ, my Savior, died for sinners just like me;
Hallelujah! Hallelujah! I'm depending on the blood.

c
In the soul-cleansing blood of the Savior,
I've been washed in the crimson flood;
Though the world may say there is hope some other way,
I'm depending on the blood.

As we look back through the ages where the kings and prophets trod,
We can see their altars flowing with the sacrificial blood,
But those types were only pointing to the promised Lamb of God;
Hallelujah! Hallelujah! I'm depending on the blood.

c
In the soul-cleansing blood of the Savior,
I've been washed in the crimson flood;
Though the world may say there is hope some other way,
I'm depending on the blood.

It's the theme of heaven's chorus, in that land of fadeless day,
That the precious blood of Jesus has washed all their sins away;
So I'll sing along life's pathway till I reach my home someday,
Hallelujah! Hallelujah! I'm depending on the blood.

c
In the soul-cleansing blood of the Savior,
I've been washed in the crimson flood;
Though the world may say there is hope some other way,
I'm depending on the blood.

120
On Calvary
Tune: "How Great Thou Art," #157
Credit: "On Calvary," J. W. MacGill; R. S. #727

It pleased the Lord to bruise His Well-Beloved
There on the cross, the cross of Calvary,
That He might pay the ransom price for sinners
And set you free from sin eternally.
He hid His face from Jesus, whom He loved
Unchangingly, eternally,
And poured on Him the wrath to sinners due,
On Calvary, dark Calvary!

Although the piercing cry went up to heaven
There on the cross, the cross of Calvary,
"My God, My God, O why didst Thou forsake Me?"
Hear Deity addressing Deity!
His God returned no answer to this cry -
Dark Calvary, how can it be!
He suffered all to set the sinner free
Through Calvary, dark Calvary!

How can you hear that cry of deepest anguish
There on the cross, the cross of Calvary,
Or watch the Savior's precious blood flow freely
At Calvary, and still impassive be?
Why would you turn from such dark grief and pain,
Such agony, borne lovingly,
Such regal grace crowned with the thorns and shame
Of Calvary, dark Calvary?

The cross unfolds God's love for guilty sinners
There on the cross, the cross of Calvary.
By it alone, such guilt can be forgiven
Eternally; what grace through Calvary!
Then trust the living Savior and you'll sing
Triumphantly of Calvary;
For heaven's song shall be eternally
Of Calvary, blest Calvary!


121
Alone

Gethsemane was a quiet garden where the Lord Jesus went just before His arrest and crucifixion (Matthew 26:36; John 18:1). His closest disciples fell asleep while He prayed alone to His Father. In agony, He expressed His willingness to suffer on the cross. He knew all that this involved, but there was no other way to remove our sins; He alone could accomplish that work.<br>Credit: "Alone"; G. H. B. #244

It was alone the Savior prayed
In dark Gethsemane,
Alone He drained the bitter cup
And suffered on the tree.

c
Alone, alone, He bore it all alone;
He gave Himself to save His own;
He suffered, bled, and died alone, alone.

It was alone the Savior stood
In Pilate's judgment hall;
Alone the crown of thorns He wore,
Forsaken there by all.

c
Alone, alone, He bore it all alone;
He gave Himself to save His own;
He suffered, bled, and died alone, alone.

Alone at Calvary He hung
That others He might save;
Forsaken there by God Himself,
Alone His life He gave.

c
Alone, alone, He bore it all alone;
He gave Himself to save His own;
He suffered, bled, and died alone, alone.

Can you reject such matchless love?
Can you His claim disown?
By faith, commit your soul to Him
Who suffered all, alone.

c
Alone, alone, He bore it all alone;
He gave Himself to save His own;
He suffered, bled, and died alone, alone.

I'll go to Him because His name,
Above all names, is Jesus.

Look, and You Will Live
Tune: "Down at the Cross," #40
In Numbers 21:5-9, God pointed dying Israelites, bitten by poisonous snakes, to the brass serpent Moses had lifted on a pole. Those who believed God looked and lived. The Lord Jesus referred to this in John 3:14, 1He said He would be lifted up on a cross and would give His life so that all who believe in Him would have eternal life.<br>Credit: "Look, and Thou Shalt Live"; C. H. F. #56

Look to the Savior on Calvary;
See how He suffered for you and me,
Bearing our judgment so lovingly.
Look, and you will live!

c
Look, and you will live!
Look, and you will live!
Look to the cross where He bled and died.
Look, and you will live!

Would you from all of your sins be free
And have salvation eternally?
Christ paid the ransom at Calvary.
Look, and you will live!

c
Look, and you will live!
Look, and you will live!
Look to the cross where He bled and died.
Look, and you will live!

Christ is the victor, as God has shown;
He sits triumphant on heaven's throne.
There is salvation in Him alone.
Look, and you will live!

c
Look, and you will live!
Look, and you will live!
Look to the cross where He bled and died.
Look, and you will live!

Life can be yours through God's risen Son;
Look to the living, ascended One!
Trust Him today, for His work is done.
Look, and you will live!

c
Look, and you will live!
Look, and you will live!
Look to the cross where He bled and died.
Look, and you will live!

Jesus from heaven will come again;
Will you go with Him or here remain?
Choose life or death; hear this glad refrain,
Look, and you will live!

c
Look, and you will live!
Look, and you will live!
Look to the cross where He bled and died.
Look, and you will live!
