I Was a Guilty Sinner
Tune: "The Cloudless Day Is Nearing" (Morning Light)
Credit: "I Was a Guilty Sinner"; C. H. F. #109

Lord Jesus Christ, my Savior, how great Thy love to me,
A love that will embrace me for all eternity!
What peace when I remember, whatever grief I see,
"I was a guilty sinner, but Jesus died for me!"

On Calvary He suffered, the Just One in my place;
I marvel at His anguish as blood flowed down His face.
Through grateful tears I worship and sing adoringly,
"I was a guilty sinner, but Jesus died for me."

He's risen and exalted, His work for sin is done,
But seated now in glory, a new work He's begun.
He lovingly will keep me secure eternally.
"I was a guilty sinner, but Jesus died for me."

When glorified in heaven, forever with the Lord,
I shall behold His glory; by all, He'll be adored;
But in that host unnumbered, my song unchanged shall be,
"I was a guilty sinner, but Jesus died for me."


142
Only Christ Can Satisfy

In John 4:13, 14, the Lord Jesus contrasts earthly joys with the satisfaction He gives: "Whosoever drinketh of this water shall thirst again: but whosoever drinketh of the water that I shall give him shall never thirst; but the water that I shall give him shall be in him a well of water springing up into everlasting life."<br>Credit: "None But Christ Can Satisfy!" B. E.; C. H. F. #140

Lord Jesus Christ, my soul has found,
And found in Thee alone,
The peace and joy I'd sought so long,
The hope I'd never known.

c
Now, only Christ can satisfy;
No other name for me!
There's love and life and lasting joy,
Lord Jesus, found in Thee.

I longed for rest and happiness
But did not turn to Thee.
I never knew the blessedness
Thy love could bring to me.

c
Now, only Christ can satisfy;
No other name for me!
There's love and life and lasting joy,
Lord Jesus, found in Thee.

I tried to find some lasting peace,
But every effort failed;
To quench the thirst within my soul
No wells on earth availed.

c
Now, only Christ can satisfy;
No other name for me!
There's love and life and lasting joy,
Lord Jesus, found in Thee.

At last my empty heart was turned
To Christ who died for me.
This loving Friend fulfills my heart
And shall eternally.

c
Now, only Christ can satisfy;
No other name for me!
There's love and life and lasting joy,
Lord Jesus, found in Thee.

For the Son of God, who came
Ruined sinners to reclaim!

Bearing shame and scoffing rude,
In my place condemned He stood,
Sealed my pardon with His blood;
Hallelujah! What a Savior!

Guilty, vile, and helpless, we;
Spotless Lamb of God was He;
Full atonement - can it be?
Hallelujah! What a Savior!

"It is finished," Jesus cried;
Now in heaven glorified,
Hallelujah! What a Savior!

All who on His Word rely;
Changed, we'll meet Him in the sky;
Hallelujah! What a Savior!

When He comes, as rightful King,
With His praise the earth will ring.
His redeemed shall ever sing,
"Hallelujah! What a Savior!"

Grace Greater Than Our Sins

The Bible emphasizes that salvation is by grace, God's unmerited favor. "For by grace are ye saved through faith; and that not of yourselves: it is the gift of God: not of works, lest any man should boast" (Ephesians 2:8, 9).<br>Credit: "Grace Greater Than Our Sins," J. H. Johnston; C. H. F. #119

Marvelous grace of our loving Lord,
Grace that exceeds our guilt and our sin!
Christ on the cross in His grace endured
All that was needed my soul to win.

c
Grace, grace, God's grace,
Grace that will pardon and cleanse within;
Grace, grace, God's grace,
Grace that is greater than all our sin.

Sin and despair, like the sea waves cold,
Threaten the soul with infinite loss;
Grace that is greater, yes, grace untold,
Points to the refuge, the mighty cross.

c
Grace, grace, God's grace,
Grace that will pardon and cleanse within;
Grace, grace, God's grace,
Grace that is greater than all our sin.

Dark is the stain that we cannot hide;
What can avail to wash it away?
Calvary's blood is a cleansing tide;
Whiter than snow you can be today.

c
Grace, grace, God's grace,
Grace that will pardon and cleanse within;
Grace, grace, God's grace,
Grace that is greater than all our sin.

Marvelous, infinite, matchless grace,
Freely bestowed on all who believe!
Guilty, accepting the sinner's place,
Will you this moment His grace receive?

c
Grace, grace, God's grace,
Grace that will pardon and cleanse within;
Grace, grace, God's grace,
Grace that is greater than all our sin.


146
O Wonderful, Wonderful Story!

The Parable of the Good Shepherd (Luke 15:4-7) gives the Lord's description of His own mission. Like that shepherd who sought the lost sheep until he found it, the Lord Jesus came to seek and to save the lost (Luke 19:10).<br>Credit: "O Wonderful, Wonderful Story!" J. M. Gray; C. H. F. #120

Missing the lost one - Shepherd true,
Coming from heaven's glory
And caring as no one else could do -
O wonderful, wonderful story!

c
O wonderful, wonderful story,
Telling His love for me!
O wonderful, wonderful story -
He's my Shepherd and ever shall be!

Seeking the scattered - Shepherd true,
Moved by profound persistence,
Enduring the pain none ever knew,
Traversing the danger and distance.

c
O wonderful, wonderful story,
Telling His love for me!
O wonderful, wonderful story -
He's my Shepherd and ever shall be!

Saving the helpless - Shepherd true,
Bearing the cross, the starkness,
Forsaken, alone, with heart pierced through,
In storm clouds of judgment and darkness.

c
O wonderful, wonderful story,
Telling His love for me!
O wonderful, wonderful story -
He's my Shepherd and ever shall be!

Healing the wounded - Shepherd true,
Cleansing away the sadness,
Assuring of blessings to ensue,
While bearing the lost home with gladness.

c
O wonderful, wonderful story,
Telling His love for me!
O wonderful, wonderful story -
He's my Shepherd and ever shall be!

Tending the faithful - Shepherd true,
Tender and kind and caring,
Providing green pastures ever new,
Then mansions above ever sharing.

c
O wonderful, wonderful story,
Telling His love for me!
O wonderful, wonderful story -
He's my Shepherd and ever shall be!

Calvary Covers It All

After King David sinned, he endured sleepless nights, an accusing conscience, and bitter tears. Repenting, he acknowledged his sin to God and later wrote, "Blessed is he whose transgression is forgiven, whose sin is covered" (Psalm 32:1).<br>Credit: "Calvary Covers It All," Mrs. W. G. Taylor; C. H. F. #59

Most dear to my heart is that I have a part
In a wealth that this world can't impart;
For the Savior alone for my sin did atone,
And Calvary covers it all.

c
Calvary covers it all,
My past with its sin and stain;
My guilt and despair
Jesus took on Him there,
And Calvary covers it all.

The stripes that He bore and the thorns that He wore
Showed His mercy and love evermore;
And my heart bowed in shame as I called on His name,
And Calvary covers it all.

c
Calvary covers it all,
My past with its sin and stain;
My guilt and despair
Jesus took on Him there,
And Calvary covers it all.

How matchless the grace, when I looked in the face
Of the Savior who died in my place;
By His payment replete my redemption's complete,
And Calvary covers it all.

c
Calvary covers it all,
My past with its sin and stain;
My guilt and despair
Jesus took on Him there,
And Calvary covers it all.

How blessed the thought, that my soul by Him bought,
To His glorious home shall be brought,
Where with gladness and song I'll be one of the throng,
And Calvary covers it all.

c
Calvary covers it all,
My past with its sin and stain;
My guilt and despair
Jesus took on Him there,
And Calvary covers it all.

149
The Solid Rock

In Matthew 7:24-27, the Lord Jesus likened obeying His Word to building a house on a solid foundation, a rock. Failing to obey His Word is like building on sand. Those who rely on Christ's Word rest on a foundation that will stand through every storm and flood.<br>Credit: "The Solid Rock," E. Mote; C. H. F. #121

My hope is built on nothing less
Than Jesus' blood and righteousness;
I dare not trust another claim,
But wholly lean on Jesus' name.

c
On Christ, the solid Rock, I stand;
All other ground is sinking sand,
All other ground is sinking sand.

When darkness seems to veil His face,
I rest on His unchanging grace;
In every raging, stormy gale,
My anchor holds and cannot fail.

c
On Christ, the solid Rock, I stand;
All other ground is sinking sand,
All other ground is sinking sand.

His Word, His promises, His blood,
Support me in life's every flood;
Should all around my soul give way,
He still will be my hope and stay.

c
On Christ, the solid Rock, I stand;
All other ground is sinking sand,
All other ground is sinking sand.

When He shall come with trumpet sound,
My praise to Him shall still resound;
Cleansed by His precious blood alone,
Faultless, I'll stand before the throne.

c
On Christ, the solid Rock, I stand;
All other ground is sinking sand,
All other ground is sinking sand.


150
My Redeemer! My Redeemer!

In a wonderful illustration of redemption, Boaz' love for Ruth caused him to pay a large sum to repurchase (redeem) her family's land. Under Hebrew law, he thus became entitled to marry her (Ruth 4). This redeemer prefigures our Lord Jesus, who paid an infinitely greater price, His blood, to claim His Bride.<br>Credit: "My Redeemer! My Redeemer!"; C. H. F. #323

My Redeemer! O what beauties
In that lovely name appear!
None but Jesus in His glories
Shall the honored title wear.
My Redeemer! My Redeemer
Ransomed me by precious blood!

Sinful, I had no perception
I was held by Satan's chain,
Guided by his skilled deception,
Rushing on to endless pain.
My Redeemer! My Redeemer
Plucked me as a brand from hell!

Mine by promise, mine forever,
Mine by oath, and mine by blood,
Nothing can this union sever,
Mine - this never-changing God.
My Redeemer! My Redeemer!
Faithful, always, ever mine!

When at last I see His glory,
At His wounded feet shall bow,
Perfect, I shall then be like Him,
And His full redemption know.
My Redeemer! My Redeemer!
Glorified, I'll sing His praise!

The blood of the cross is my only foundation,
The death of my Savior sufficient alone.

c

Can purchase peace of mind,
For conscience points to inward sin
And guilty deeds combined.
It's only through the blood of Christ
A guilty soul can find
That lasting peace and liberty
Which God Himself designed.

c
It's joyous news! It's blessed news!
The Savior's precious blood
Can cleanse the guilty from his sin
And give him peace with God.

What was the dying thief's request,
The blessing most required?
Was it his friends or wealth or fame
As life's brief day expired?
"O Lord, remember me," he cried
To Jesus on the tree.
Christ gave His word, thus gave him peace
To face eternity.

c
It's joyous news! It's blessed news!
The Savior's precious blood
Can cleanse the guilty from his sin
And give him peace with God.

What joy can equal peace with God,
Or what could greater be,
Than knowing that the soul is safe
For all eternity,
Safe in the Lord, the conscience calmed,
Now cleansed within, without?
The Savior's blood removes all stains;
His Word removes all doubt.

c
It's joyous news! It's blessed news!
The Savior's precious blood
Can cleanse the guilty from his sin
And give him peace with God.

It Is Finished

"Christ Jesus came into the world to save sinners" (1 Timothy 1:15). After suffering on the cross for our sins, Jesus cried with a loud voice, "It is finished!" Sin's debt was paid in full.<br>Credit: "It Is Finished," J. Proctor; C. H. F. #128

Nothing we can do will save us,
Nothing we can pay;
Nothing but the blood of Jesus
Washes sins away.

c
"It is finished!" He decreed it!
He is God, the Son.
Finished! Nothing more is needed;
All the work is done!

Christ descended, leaving heaven
For the cross of shame,
That our sins might be forgiven;
This is why He came!

c
"It is finished!" He decreed it!
He is God, the Son.
Finished! Nothing more is needed;
All the work is done!

Weary, with your strength depleted,
Yearning, peace to know,
Hear Him! All has been completed
Many years ago.

c
"It is finished!" He decreed it!
He is God, the Son.
Finished! Nothing more is needed;
All the work is done!

End your efforts; He has spoken,
God's beloved Son,
And His pledge cannot be broken;
Trust Him, it is done!

c
"It is finished!" He decreed it!
He is God, the Son.
Finished! Nothing more is needed;
All the work is done!

Let your pointless toil be ended;
Rest in Christ, the Lord;
He saves all who have depended
On His faithful Word.

c
"It is finished!" He decreed it!
He is God, the Son.
Finished! Nothing more is needed;
All the work is done!


154
Give Me Just a Little Longer

Credit: "Give Me Just a Little Longer"; C. H. F. #229

Now's the time to take salvation;
Hear the Savior's call today.
He is waiting; He will save you.
What a sad mistake to say,
"Give me just a little longer,
For my future seems so bright;
When I think that I am dying
I'll be saved, but not tonight!"

When God's judgment overtakes you,
Will your answer then seem right?
You'll recall the Savior's pleading
And your final, "Not tonight."
Then, no time to change your answer,
Then, no time to count the cost,
Then, no hope amid the darkness,
You will be forever lost.

How misguided is the thinking
That the Lord your time will wait!
Millions have been lost forever,
Just outside salvation's gate.
Once, the Savior urged them also,
"Strive to enter in this night,"
But, like you, they gave their answer,
"I'll be saved, but not tonight!"

Listen to the loving Savior,
Pleading with you patiently.
Listen to His kind entreaty,
As He calls, "Come unto Me."
Turn away from Satan's whispers,
Though his promises seem bright;
Answer Jesus, gladly saying,
"I'll be saved; I'll come tonight."

Verily, Verily

"Verily, Verily," spoken by the Lord Jesus, is a double affirmation. It could be translated, "It is true; it is true." This appears 25 times in John's gospel.<br>Credit: "Verily, Verily," J. McGranahan; C. H. F. #141

O what a Savior, that He died for me!
From condemnation He has set me free;
"He that believeth on the Son," said He,
"Hath everlasting life."

c
"Verily, verily, I say unto you,"
"Verily, verily," message ever new,
"He that believeth on the Son," it's true,
"Hath everlasting life."

All my iniquities on Him were laid;
All my indebtedness by Him was paid;
All who believe on Him, the Lord has said,
Have everlasting life.

c
"Verily, verily, I say unto you,"
"Verily, verily," message ever new,
"He that believeth on the Son," it's true,
"Hath everlasting life."

Though I'm unworthy, I can trust the Lord;
Though I am sinful, I can trust His Word.
"He that believeth on the Son of God

c

"Hath everlasting life."

He that believes on Him, there is no doubt,
Has everlasting life.

c
"Verily, verily, I say unto you,"
"Verily, verily," message ever new,

O Wondrous Grace
Tune: "Come, Let Us Sing the Matchless Worth"
Credit: "O Wondrous Grace"; S. G. H. #72

Our God in grace designed a plan
To rescue guilty, fallen man
And save his priceless soul;
God "found a ransom" in His Son;
Christ died for sins - His work is done.
Let all such grace extol!

What splendid grace, divine and free!
The Savior faced the penalty;
Now God is satisfied.
His Son endured the curse, the loss,
The wrath of God, the shameful cross,
When for the lost He died.

"To every creature," every race,
God sends the gospel of His grace
And offers life today.
The blood of Jesus Christ His Son,
By whom the saving work was done,
Can cleanse your sins away.

How foolish if you should refuse
The gospel's liberating news,
The chains of sin embrace!
How swiftly life is passing by!
How tragic in your sins to die,
Rejecting saving grace!

170
Jesus, I Come

Matthew, Mark, and Luke all recount the story of a deranged man who lived among the tombs, terrorized the neighborhood, and could not be captured. When the Lord visited his region, the man came to Him and was delivered. The transformed man was now "sitting, clothed, and in his right mind" (Mark 5:11). This pictures the spiritual blessings given to all who come to the Lord today.<br>Credit: "Jesus, I Come," W. T. Sleeper; C. H. F. #242

Out of my bondage, sorrow, and night,
Jesus, I come! Jesus, I come!
Into Thy freedom, gladness, and light,
Jesus, I come to Thee!
Out of my darkness, sin, and disgrace,
Out of my guilt Thy blood can efface,
Out of my sin and into Thy grace,
Jesus, I come to Thee!

Out of my shameful failure and loss,
Jesus, I come! Jesus, I come!
All that I need bestowed at the cross,
Jesus, I come to Thee!
Out of my shame for what I have been,
Out of my stains, to cleansing within,
Out of my guilt, to pardon from sin,
Jesus, I come to Thee!

Out of the fear and dread of the tomb,
Jesus, I come! Jesus, I come!
Into the joy and light of Thy home,
Jesus, I come to Thee!
Out of the depths of ruin untold,
Into the peace and rest of Thy fold,
Ever Thy blessed face to behold,
Jesus, I come to Thee!

Pass Me Not

As the crowd passed by, blind Bartimaeus called loudly and persistently for Jesus of Nazareth to have mercy on him. Jesus gave him his sight. Bartimaeus embraced this golden opportunity, his last, because soon afterward, Jesus was crucified (Mark 10:46-52).<br>Credit: "Pass Me Not," F. J. Crosby; C. H. F. #238

Pass me not, O gentle Savior;
Hear my humble cry;
While on others Thou art calling,
Do not pass me by.

c
Savior, Savior, hear my humble cry;
While on others Thou art calling,
Do not pass me by.

In Thy tender grace and mercy,
Hear my heart's request;
As I kneel in deep contrition,
Give my conscience rest.

c
Savior, Savior, hear my humble cry;
While on others Thou art calling,
Do not pass me by.

Trusting only in Thy merit
Would I seek Thy face;
Heal my wounded, broken spirit;
Save me by Thy grace.

c
Savior, Savior, hear my humble cry;
While on others Thou art calling,
Do not pass me by.

Savior, source of joy and comfort,
More than all to me,
When the storms of life have ended,
I shall be with Thee.

c
Savior, Savior, hear my humble cry;
While on others Thou art calling,
Do not pass me by.

Where eternal rest is found?
Passing onward, passing onward,
Can you tell me where you're bound?

Soon your life will pass away.
God has said the saved are going
To a world of perfect day,
Passing onward, passing onward!
Christ their Leader, Christ their Way.

Many on the downward road,
Careless of their soul's salvation,
Heeding not the call of God,
Passing onward, passing onward,
Disregarding Jesus' blood.

Passing onward, quickly passing!
Time its course will quickly run;
Do not slight the fond entreaty
Of the ever-gracious One.
Come and trust Him; come and trust Him;
All His work to save is done.

c

"Turn or you'll perish in hell's dark abode!"

c
Rescue the perishing! Bring them to Jesus;
Tell them these words of hope: Jesus can save!


180
Rock of Ages

Isaiah wrote in Isaiah 26:4 that the Lord was to be trusted because in Him was "everlasting strength." The Hebrew words for "everlasting strength" can be literally translated as "a Rock of Ages."<br>Credit: "Rock of Ages," A. M. Toplady; C. H. F. #148

Rock of Ages, cleft for me,
I must hide myself in Thee.
There the precious, cleansing blood,
From Thy wounded side which flowed,
Saves me from the guilt of sin,
From its mastery within.

Nothing done by sinful hands
Can fulfill Thy Law's demands.
Could my zeal no respite know,
Contrite tears abundant flow,
All for sin could not atone;
Thou must save, and Thou alone.

Nothing in my hand I bring;
Simply to Thy cross I cling;
Hopeless and in deep distress,
Helpless, thankful for Thy grace,
Hungry, thirsty, I can see
Every need is met in Thee.

When I draw my final breath,
Should my journey end in death,
I will soar to worlds unknown
And will praise Thee on Thy throne.
Rock of Ages, cleft for me,
I have hid myself in Thee!

To hear His patient knocking nevermore.

His father gave him a gracious and lavish welcome, as God does with all repentant sinners (Luke 15).<br>Credit: "Christ Receiveth Sinful Men," E. F. Bevan; C. H. F. #158

196
Tears Overflowed the Savior's Heart
Tune: "To Calvary, Lord" (Martyrdom)
About a week before His crucifixion and just before His triumphal entry into Jerusalem (sometimes called Salem), our Lord wept profusely. He knew that, although He offered His people peace and blessing and they would acclaim Him as King, they also would soon cry, "We have no king but Caesar." He would be crucified beneath the title, "King of the Jews." He alone knew the resulting devastation this would mean for His beloved city.

Tears overflowed the Savior's heart;
Dark storm clouds loomed ahead.
He offered Salem peace that day;
They chose God's wrath instead.

Tears fill the eyes of those who care,
But you this choice must make,
New life and heaven's endless joys
Or judgment's storm-tossed lake.

Tears, blood-like sweat dropped to the dust;
Christ knew the storm He'd face,
The awesome price for Him, the Lamb,
To suffer in our place.

Your tears of joy would overflow,
Your storm of conscience cease,
If, in your sins, you'd come to Christ
And enter into peace.

But tears would never cease in hell,
While waves of judgment roll,
If you should choose to die in sin
And lose your priceless soul.

Write on my heart every word;
Tell me that truth I hold precious,
Greatest that ever was heard.

"Glory to God in the highest!
Peace and good tidings to earth!"

c

Write on my heart every word;
Tell me the story most precious,
Sweetest that ever was heard.

Fasting alone in the desert
Tells of the days that He passed,
How He was tried and was tempted,
Yet was triumphant at last.
Tell of the years of His labor,
Tell of the sorrows He bore;
He was despised and afflicted,
Homeless, rejected, and poor.

c

Write on my heart every word;
Tell me the story most precious,
Sweetest that ever was heard.

Bleeding, in sorrow and pain;
Tell of the grave where they laid Him;
Tell how He lives once again.
Love, in that story so tender,
Clearer than ever I see,
Love for the guilty and helpless;
Love for a sinner like me.

c
Tell me the story of Jesus,
Write on my heart every word;
Tell me the story most precious,
Sweetest that ever was heard.

"Whosoever" is a word often used in the Bible to include everyone. Significantly, God gives this invitation just as the Bible closes, "Whosoever will, let him take the water of life freely" (Revelation 22:17).<br>Credit: "That Grand Word, Whosoever," E. E. Hewitt; C. H. F. #163

That grand word, whosoever, is ringing through my soul,
"Whosoever will may come."
In rivers of salvation, the living waters roll,
"Whosoever will may come."

c
O that whosoever!
"Whosoever will may come."
The Savior's invitation is freely sounding still,
"Whosoever will may come."

Whenever this glad message in God's own Word I see,
"Whosoever will may come,"
I know it's meant for sinners, I know it's meant for me,
"Whosoever will may come."

c
O that whosoever!
"Whosoever will may come."
The Savior's invitation is freely sounding still,
"Whosoever will may come."

I heard the loving message and now to others say,
"Whosoever will may come."
Seek now this living Savior and He'll be yours today;
"Whosoever will may come."

c
O that whosoever!
"Whosoever will may come."
The Savior's invitation is freely sounding still,
"Whosoever will may come."

To God be all the glory, His only Son He gave,
"Whosoever will may come,"
And those who come believing, He will forever save;
"Whosoever will may come."

c
O that whosoever!
"Whosoever will may come."
The Savior's invitation is freely sounding still,
"Whosoever will may come."

The Blood of Jesus Ransomed Me

Credit: "The Blood of Jesus Ransomed Me," M. E. Gregory; C. H. F. #164

The blessed peace of Christ my conscience stills;
His reconciling work I see;
His love divine my joyous spirit thrills,
For Jesus' blood has ransomed me.

c
The blood of Jesus ransomed me;
He paid my debt and set me free;
Where'er I go, the world shall know
The blood of Jesus ransomed me.

He floods my pathway with celestial light;
He caused my blinded eyes to see;
From Satan's power and from sin's dark night
The blood of Jesus ransomed me.

c
The blood of Jesus ransomed me;
He paid my debt and set me free;
Where'er I go, the world shall know
The blood of Jesus ransomed me.

His grace preserves me from the tempter's dart
And gives me strength to meet the foe;
He now resides within my grateful heart;
He's with me everywhere I go.

c
The blood of Jesus ransomed me;
He paid my debt and set me free;
Where'er I go, the world shall know
The blood of Jesus ransomed me.

When I shall walk with Him on earth no more,
In heaven, I His face shall see;
I'll sing His praises on that blissful shore
And tell how Jesus ransomed me.

c
The blood of Jesus ransomed me;
He paid my debt and set me free;
Where'er I go, the world shall know
The blood of Jesus ransomed me.

At the Cross

Credit: "At the Cross"; G. H. B. #117

The cross! The cross! The wondrous cross!
There Christ, the Savior, died;
I see His shame, His thorn-clad brow,
His pierced and bleeding side.

c
At the cross! At the cross, where I first saw the light,
And the burden of my heart rolled away,
It was there by faith I received my sight,
And now I am thankful every day.

I see the burden of my sin
The Lord on Him has laid,
And He, the spotless Lamb of God,
My sacrifice was made.

c
At the cross! At the cross, where I first saw the light,
And the burden of my heart rolled away,
It was there by faith I received my sight,
And now I am thankful every day.

The cross of Christ is all my boast,
His blood my only plea;
My passport to the realms of bliss
Is "Jesus died for me."

c
At the cross! At the cross, where I first saw the light,
And the burden of my heart rolled away,
It was there by faith I received my sight,
And now I am thankful every day.


204
Jesus, the Lamb
Tune: "Haven of Rest"
Christ was introduced as the Lamb: "Behold the Lamb of God, which taketh away the sin of the world" (John 1:29). Centuries before, Jeremiah asked a question that reminds us of Christ's sufferings for sins: "Is it nothing to you, all ye that pass by? Behold, and see if there be any sorrow like unto My sorrow" (Lamentations 1:12).

The crowds press along, passing Calvary's Lamb
With thorns as His rude diadem;
They mock and they curse the eternal I AM;
His sorrow means nothing to them.
His love for the lost is confining Him there,
Not nails or the power of men;
"My Father, forgive them"; how tender His prayer!
Yet Jesus means nothing to them.

c
Could Jesus, the Lamb, still mean nothing to you?
While passing Him, stop and behold;
To bear for your sins all the wrath that was due,
He's suffering sorrows untold.

The darkness envelops the Lamb on the tree;
How deep the distress suffered then!
"My God, O My God, why didst Thou forsake Me?"
His anguish means nothing to them.
Alone in His sorrow, surrounded by grief,
"I thirst," Jesus cries out again;
They offer no pity; they bring no relief,
For Jesus means nothing to them.

c
Could Jesus, the Lamb, still mean nothing to you?
While passing Him, stop and behold;
To bear for your sins all the wrath that was due,
He's suffering sorrows untold.

The cup He has drained and provision is made,
Sufficient for all sinful men;
He cried, "It is finished," the debt has been paid;
His triumph means nothing to them.
His arms are extended, to all they implore;
Yet most still this Savior condemn.
His wounds make them welcome inside heaven's door,
But Jesus means nothing to them.

c
Could Jesus, the Lamb, still mean nothing to you?
While passing Him, stop and behold;
To bear for your sins all the wrath that was due,
He's suffering sorrows untold.

The Glory of the Greatest Gift
Tune: "I Bow Me to Thy Will" (Arlington) (repeat line 3)<br>Alt. Tune: "Now, Only Christ Can Satisfy," #142 (join 2 verses)<br>Alt. Tune with chorus: "Happy Wanderer"


The glory of the greatest gift
Shines out at Calvary;
God gave His Well-Beloved Son
To suffer on a tree.

The summit of the greatest love
Was reached at Calvary;
Our Maker for our sins came down
To die in agony.

The cleansing for the greatest sins
Flows out from Calvary;
The blood of Jesus Christ God's Son
Can set the guilty free.

The sunrise of the greatest joy
Will dawn at Calvary
When you receive the Son of God,
Who paid sin's penalty.

The pathway to the greatest loss
Descends past Calvary;
For all must still reject such love
To perish endlessly.

The crossroads of the greatest choice
Still meet at Calvary;
There each for heaven or for hell
Decides his destiny.

c
<b><i>CHORUS FOR ALTERNATE TUNE:</i></b>
Son of God! Bearing sin on the tree!
It's the wonder of the ages! Can it be
That He loved and gave Himself for me!


206
The Gospel of God's Grace

In John 3:14,15, the Lord Jesus explained how Nicodemus could receive everlasting life. Jesus referred to the occasion when Moses placed a brass serpent on a pole. Israelites who had been bitten by poisonous serpents were told to look to this divinely selected remedy in order to live. Those who believed God's promise looked and lived. Similarly, the Lord Jesus said He would be lifted up at Calvary so that perishing sinners would have everlasting life by believing in Him.<br>Credit: "The Gospel of Thy Grace," A. T. Pierson; C. H. F. #165

The gospel of God's grace! By this my heart was won;
For God so loved the world, He gave His only Son,
That whosoever will believe shall everlasting life receive,
Shall everlasting life receive.

The serpent lifted up could life and healing give,
So Jesus on the cross tells me to look and live,
That whosoever will believe shall everlasting life receive,
Shall everlasting life receive.

"The soul that sinneth dies"; my awful doom I heard;
I was forever lost, but for God's gracious Word
That whosoever will believe shall everlasting life receive,
Shall everlasting life receive.

"Not to condemn the world" the Man of Sorrows came,
But that the world might have salvation through His name,
For whosoever will believe shall everlasting life receive,
Shall everlasting life receive.

210
The Love of God

Credit: "The Love of God," F. M. Lehman; M. M. #241

The love of God is greater far
Than tongue or pen can ever tell;
It goes beyond the highest star
And reaches to the gates of hell.
Rebellious man - amazing plan -
God gave His Son to win;
The most defiled, when reconciled,
Are cleansed from all their sin.

c
O love of God, how rich and pure!
How measureless and strong!
It shall forevermore endure,
Our everlasting song.

Could we with ink the ocean fill
And were the skies of parchment made,
Were every stalk on earth a quill
And every man a scribe by trade,
To write the love of God above
Would drain the ocean dry,
Nor could the scroll contain the whole,
Though stretched from sky to sky.

c
O love of God, how rich and pure!
How measureless and strong!
It shall forevermore endure,
Our everlasting song.

When time at last shall pass away
And earthly thrones and kingdoms fall,
When those who here refuse to pray
Will on the rocks and mountains call,
God's love, so sure, shall still endure,
Eternal, boundless, strong;
Redeeming grace to Adam's race
Will be our endless song.

c
O love of God, how rich and pure!
How measureless and strong!
It shall forevermore endure,
Our everlasting song.

213
The Ninety and Nine

In Luke 15, the Lord Jesus told about a shepherd who searched for a lost sheep until he found it. The Savior deftly painted the picture of His own mission, the tremendous demands of His cross, and the limitless sacrifice He would willingly make.<br>Credit: "The Ninety and Nine," E. C. Clephane; C. H. F. #175

The ninety and nine complacent lay
Within the good Shepherd's fold,
But one that was lost had gone astray;
Its danger could not be told -
Away on the mountains wild and bare,
Away from the tender Shepherd's care,
Away from the tender Shepherd's care.

"Lord, still there are here these ninety-nine;
Are they not enough for Thee?"
But grieving, He'd sighed, "This sheep of Mine
Has wandered away from Me,
And though the ravines are rough and steep,
I'll search till I find My one lost sheep.
I'll search till I find My one lost sheep."

No mortal can know - yet He foreknew -
The wrath of the floods He crossed,
The storm and the darkness He passed through
To tenderly lift the lost.
But over the winds, He heard its cry,
So helpless, so weak, and soon to die,
So helpless, so weak, and soon to die.

"Lord, why do these blood-drops stain the way,
Retracing the rugged track?"
"They flowed for the one who went astray
To find him and bring him back."
"Lord, why is Thy brow so pierced and torn?"
"It's marred by the sharp and painful thorn.
It's marred by the sharp and painful thorn."

But all through the mountains, thunder-riv'n,
And up through the rocky steep,
There rises a cry that rolls through heav'n,
"Rejoice! I have found My sheep!"
The angels respond around the throne,
"Rejoice, for the Lord brings back His own!
Rejoice, for the Lord brings back His own!"


214
The Perfect Righteousness of God
Tune: "Redemption Ground," #33
Credit: "The Perfect Righteousness of God," A. Midlane; G. T. H. B. #172

The perfect righteousness of God
Is witnessed in the Savior's blood,
For in the cross of Christ we trace
God's righteousness, His love, and grace.
God could not overlook our sin
And then to heaven bring us in,
But in the cross of Christ we see
How He can save us righteously.

On Christ the weight of sin was laid,
And by His blood sin's debt was paid.
Stern Justice can demand no more;
Christ's work has made salvation sure.
The sinner who believes is free,
Can say, "The Savior died for me,"
Can point to the atoning blood
And say, "This made my peace with God."

The Righteous God of Heaven
Tune: "The Cloudless Day Is Nearing" (Morning Light)
Credit: "The Righteous God of Heaven," J. L. Parks

The righteous God of Heaven extends His hand in love;
He welcomes men and women to live with Him above.
Though sins have made us distant and hid His holy face,
The righteous God of Heaven still reaches out in grace.

How helpless our condition! We stand condemned by sin;
We cannot buy salvation or work our way to Him.
We can't effect our pardon, though we might do our best;
The righteous God of Heaven still kindly offers rest.

The righteous God of Heaven, in matchless love to man,
To pardon our transgressions designed salvation's plan;
The price that He required was paid in drops of blood;
The One who paid the ransom was Christ, the Son of God.

In Christ, who died for sinners, God's righteousness is shown,
For Jesus bore the judgment, endured sin's curse alone.
The righteous God of Heaven now points to Him, the Way;
Then trust this living Savior, and you'll be saved today!

The Voice of the Lord
Tune: "Hiding in Thee" (Security, without chorus)<br>Alt. Tune: "How Firm a Foundation" (Foundation)
In Ezekiel 33, the Lord portrays His messenger, the prophet Ezekiel, as a watchman, who was to awaken God's people to the danger of His judgment.<br>Credit: "'Tis the Voice of Jehovah"; G. H. B. #140

The voice of the Lord kindly calls you, "Awake!"
Eternity's coming; your soul is at stake.
How swiftly life passes; the moments speed by!
Then turn or you'll perish; awake, hear His cry!

Awake, if you're thinking God's favor is won
By works of religion or deeds you have done!
We all are unclean in God's pure, holy eye.
Then turn or you'll perish; awake, hear His cry!

Awake, if you're careless, for all is not well;
The road that you travel is leading to hell!
Sin's pleasures are passing and soon you could die;
Then turn or you'll perish; awake, hear His cry!

Awake, if you have a concern for your soul!
Let nothing deter you; press on to the goal!
What sorrow forever, should Christ pass you by!
Then turn or you'll perish; awake, hear His cry!

If you've been awakened, respond to God's Word,
Proclaiming salvation through Jesus the Lord.
He offered Himself all your sin-debt to pay;
Turn now to the Savior; He'll save you today.

Is flowing freely to us now.

The value of the blood,
So rudely shed by man,
Has met the claims of God.
Why stand we then without in fear?
The blood of Christ invites us near.

The new and living way

Our present and our endless home.

His precious blood once shed
Has made and keeps us clean;
With calm assurance we draw near;
His blood has banished all our fear.

Then to the Lamb once slain
Be praise and majesty!
He died and lives again;
He lives eternally,
Who loved us, cleansed us by His blood,
And "made us kings and priests to God."


220
What Will You Do with Jesus?

Pilate was the Roman judge who tried the Lord Jesus (Matthew 27:22). During the trial, he asked, "What shall I do then with Jesus?" Bowing to political pressure, he delivered the Lord Jesus to be crucified. If only he had accepted Jesus as his Lord and Savior, how different Pilate's eternal destiny would have been!<br>Credit: "What Will You Do with Jesus?" N. Norton; C. H. F. #233

"Then what shall I do with Jesus?"
Once asked in Pilate's hall,
It still confronts each person
Who hears the gospel's call,
For this one choice determines
Your home eternally;
Then, what will you do with Jesus?
O what will your answer be?

c
What will your answer be?
What will your answer be?
What will you do with Jesus?
O what will your answer be?

"Then what shall I do with Jesus?"
He left His home above,
In lowly grace descending,
That you might share His love;
His blood was shed for sinners
In shame and agony.
Then, what will you do with Jesus?
O what will your answer be?

c
What will your answer be?
What will your answer be?
What will you do with Jesus?
O what will your answer be?

"Then what shall I do with Jesus?"
The gospel's call is clear;
The Lord now longs to free you
From every sin and fear;
For this He came from heaven
To die on Calvary;
Then, what will you do with Jesus?
O what will your answer be?

c
What will your answer be?
What will your answer be?
What will you do with Jesus?
O what will your answer be?

"Then what shall I do with Jesus?"
Yes, you must count the cost;
To trust Him means salvation;
Without Him, you'll be lost.
Your soul must face the question
Of your own destiny;
Then, what will you do with Jesus?
O what will your answer be?

c
What will your answer be?
What will your answer be?
What will you do with Jesus?
O what will your answer be?

Wash all my sins away.

c

From sin to set me free.

From heaven turn away.

From sin to set me free.

Shall be our endless theme.

That Jesus died for me,

From sin to set me free.

If His death all my debt has not paid?

c

c

c
Look! Look! Look and live!

Just believe it!"

I believed it!

Just believe it!

O believe it! O believe it!

With joy I will await the day
I see my Lord.

And all I have flows from the truth
That Jesus lives.

Sins As Scarlet

The prophet Isaiah recorded many of God's greatest promises to Israel. He promised that if they returned to God, He would have mercy on them; if they would look in faith to God, He would save them; if they would come to God, He would wash away their sins.<br>Credit: "Sins As Scarlet," F. J. Crosby; R. S. #94

Though your sins are as scarlet, they shall be as white as snow;
Though your sins are as scarlet, they shall be as white as snow;
Though they are red like crimson, they shall be as wool.
Though your sins are as scarlet, though your sins are as scarlet,
They shall be as white as snow; they shall be as white as snow.

Hear the voice that entreats you, "Now return again to God!"
Hear the voice that entreats you, "Now return again to God!"
He calls with great compassion and abounding love.
Hear the voice that entreats you, hear the voice that entreats you,
"Now return again to God!" "Now return again to God!"

He'll forgive your transgressions and remember them no more;
He'll forgive your transgressions and remember them no more;
"Look unto Me, ye people," says the Lord your God.
He'll forgive your transgressions, He'll forgive your transgressions,
And remember them no more, and remember them no more.

Time Is Earnest
Tune: "Have Thine Own Way" (Modified)<br>Alt. Tune: "O Our Savior" (Nottingham)
Credit: "Time Is Earnest," J. Montgomery; C. H. F. #237

Time is earnest, passing by;
Death is earnest, drawing nigh.
Don't be careless, while today
Hopes of heaven drift away.

Life is earnest, soon it's past;
Hell or heaven come at last.
You must face eternity!
Will you never earnest be?

God, in earnest, calls to you;
We are earnest, pleading, too.
While His Spirit strives anew,
You must choose; what will you do?

Earnestly the Savior cried,
"It is finished!" when He died.
Hear His word, for Jesus' blood
Meets the holy claims of God!

Be in earnest; choose today!
Quickly time will pass away!
Now's the time to count the cost;
Then, though earnest, you'll be lost.

Is My Name Written There?

The Lord Jesus told His disciples to rejoice that their names were "written in heaven." The Book of Revelation records that those whose names are written in the Lamb's book of life will live forever with God, while those whose names are missing will be cast into "the lake of fire."<br>Credit: "Lord, I Care Not for Riches," M. A. K.; C. H. F. #116

To be certain of heaven would be worth more than gold;
Yet to enter those mansions, in the Bible we're told
That a new birth is needed; this we can't overlook,
We must have our name written in the Lamb's sacred book.

c
Is my name written there 
On the pages so fair?
In the Lamb's book in heaven,
Is my name written there?

No defilement can enter heaven's city of light,
Yet I know I am sinful as I stand in God's sight.
For my name to be listed in that book, I must know
That my sins, though like scarlet, have been washed "white as snow."

c
Is my name written there 
On the pages so fair?
In the Lamb's book in heaven,
Is my name written there?

I've no plea for my cleansing, but the Lamb's precious blood.
I've no other assurance, but what's written by God.
He who gives me His promise in the Scriptures down here
Wrote my name on the pages of that book over there.

c
Yes, my name's written there
On the pages so fair;
In the Lamb's book in heaven,
Yes, my name's written there.

In that beautiful city, with its glory so bright,
Where the Lord God is dwelling and the Lamb is the light,
Where the saints gone before us join forever to share
In the singing of heaven, yes, my name's written there.

c
Yes, my name's written there
On the pages so fair;
In the Lamb's book in heaven,
Yes, my name's written there.

Till I see His face in glory;
Hallelujah! Jesus ransomed me!

Tune: "Jehovah Tsidkenu" (Clarendon Street), #97<br>Alt. Tune: "Lord Jesus, I Love Thee" (Affection)
The prophet Ezekiel warned his people that God's judgment on their sins would result in death. Ezekiel 33:11 quotes God's wish: "As I live, saith the Lord God, I have no pleasure in the death of the wicked." He appealed, "Turn ye, turn ye from your evil ways; for why will ye die, O house of Israel?"<br>Credit: "O Turn Ye!" J. Hopkins; R. S. #176

Turn now to the Savior, for why will you die,
While God in His grace calls from heaven on high?
Now Jesus invites you, the Spirit says come,
The Father is waiting to welcome you home.

How vain the deception that you'll find a way
To help your condition! Why will you delay?
Come guilty, unworthy; His mercy is free;
The price of salvation was paid on the tree.

In riches, in pleasure, what will you obtain
To quiet your conscience or banish life's pain,
To comfort your heart as death's cold waters roll,
Assure you of heaven, bright home of the soul?

The Savior has promised your soul to receive
And pardon you freely; His promise believe!
If sin is your burden, why will you not come?
He waits to receive you; He bids you come home.

Was It for Me?

Some who hear the gospel do not personally benefit from its message. Those who receive its benefits recognize that the cross of Christ involved them personally. Like the apostle Paul, they know "The Son of God . . . loved me, and gave Himself for me" (Galatians 2:20).<br>Credit: "Was It for Me?" J. M. Whyte; C. H. F. #194

Was it for me, for me alone,
The Savior left His lofty throne,
The dazzling splendors of the sky?
Was it for me He came to die?

c
It was for me, yes, all for me;
O love of God, so great, so free!
Amazing love, I'll gladly sing,
"He died for me, my Lord, the King."

Was it for me angelic praise
Enthralled those lowly shepherds' gaze
That starlit night so long ago?
Was it for me God planned it so?

c
It was for me, yes, all for me;
O love of God, so great, so free!
Amazing love, I'll gladly sing,
"He died for me, my Lord, the King."

Was it for me He wept and prayed,
While blood-like sweat His grief conveyed?
That night within Gethsemane,
Was it for me, that agony?

c
It was for me, yes, all for me;
O love of God, so great, so free!
Amazing love, I'll gladly sing,
"He died for me, my Lord, the King."

Was it for me He bowed His head
On Calvary, and freely shed
His precious blood, that crimson tide?
Was it for me the Savior died?

c
It was for me, yes, all for me;
O love of God, so great, so free!
Amazing love, I'll gladly sing,
"He died for me, my Lord, the King."

Was it for me He said He'll come
And take me to the Father's home?
This is the promise of His Word:
I'll be forever with the Lord.

c
It was for me, yes, all for me;
O love of God, so great, so free!
Amazing love, I'll gladly sing,
"He died for me, my Lord, the King."

In the story of the Passover (Exodus 12), God required all the families in Egypt to sprinkle a lamb's blood at the entrance of their home. God promised that every home marked by blood was safe from judgment. The blood provided shelter; His word, assuring them of safety, gave them rest.

Resting, resting, 
Resting on the changeless Word of God!

Now there's no weight of guilt on me.

That Jesus took so willingly.

Now there's no judgment left for me.

Now all God's favor shines on me.

And I am blest through that stark tree;
For me, the Prince of Life has died
To give me life eternally.
When, at His side, I'm glorified,
I'll owe it all to Calvary.

255
Jesus of Nazareth
Alt. Tune: "Eternity, Time Soon Will End," #43
Bartimaeus, outside the city of Jericho, and Zacchaeus, inside, realized that Jesus' visit to their city was their one chance to obtain His blessing. Saved by faith, they rejoiced in the assurance of salvation they had received from "Jesus of Nazareth" (Luke 18:35-43; 19:1-10).<br>Credit: "Jesus of Nazareth," E. Campbell; R. S. #256

What gathers this expectant throng?
On dusty paths they pass along,
While pressing on Him day by day
To follow all He has to say.
Amazed, they give this hushed reply,
"Jesus of Nazareth passes by."

Who is this Jesus? Can it be,
He was the Lord eternally,
The Father's Well-Beloved Son,
By whom creation's work was done?
Of Him, the lowly One, they cry,
"Jesus of Nazareth passes by."

He speaks; more gracious is His word
Than anything they've ever heard.
His mighty power heals the lame,
The blind, the sick - to all the same.
The golden moments testify,
"Jesus of Nazareth passes by."

The blind man all the tumult hears;
He cries, insistent, as Christ nears.
And short Zacchaeus climbs a tree;
The passing Savior he must see.
This was their day of blessing. Why?
"Jesus of Nazareth passes by."

How many others missed their day,
When Jesus moved along that way.
How tragic! They would later learn
That Jesus never would return.
Too late they lifted up their cry,
"Jesus of Nazareth had passed by."

To all the heavy-laden, come!
There's pardon, comfort, rest, and home;
The Savior has prepared a place;
Come now, accept His offered grace;
Now on His faithful Word rely;
"Jesus of Nazareth passes by."

But if you will this call refuse
And all His patient love abuse,
Soon He will sadly from you turn,
Your anxious prayer for mercy spurn.
"Too late! Too late!" will be the cry,
"Jesus of Nazareth has passed by."

What Will You Do in That Great Day?
Tune: "Jesus of Nazareth," #255 (Modified)<br>Alt. Tune: "Eternity, Time Soon Will End," #43

When earth and sky shall pass away,
When all the pomp and glory here
Like morning dew shall disappear,
When, risen from your lonely tomb,
You'll stand in judgment's awful doom?

When God's great trump shall wake the dead,
You'll meet your God with solemn dread.
What will you do? Where can you go
Amid that fearful scene of woe,
Where none can help and all alone
You stand before that great white throne?

And then where will you find retreat?
There is no shelter anymore,
For death and hell their dead restore.

Sheltered, O Lamb of God, in Thee,
Safe at Thy side when piercing, loud,
The cries of that unnumbered crowd
Shall rend the heavens, fill the skies,
Till judgment's doom engulfs their cries!

263
It Is Well with My Soul

In 2 Kings 4:26, a mother whose son had died went to Elisha the prophet. Asked, "Is it well with thee?" she expressed her confidence in God by answering, "It is well" (meaning, "Everything is all right"). The writer of this hymn borrowed those words and penned "It Is Well with My Soul" when he received the news that his four daughters had lost their lives at sea.<br>Credit: "It Is Well with My Soul," H. G. Spafford; C. H. F. #386

When peace, like a river, is flowing my way,
When sorrows, like sea-billows, roll,
Whatever I face, Thou hast taught me to say,
"It is well, it is well with my soul."

c
It is well with my soul,
It is well, it is well with my soul.

Though Satan attack me, though trials should come,
Let this calm assurance control,
That Christ has regarded my helpless estate
And has shed His own blood for my soul.

c
It is well with my soul,
It is well, it is well with my soul.

My sin - O the bliss of this glorious thought!
My sin, not in part, but the whole,
Was nailed to His cross and I bear it no more;
Praise the Lord, praise the Lord, O my soul!

c
It is well with my soul,
It is well, it is well with my soul.

For me be it Christ, be it Christ now to live;
Though death's waves around me should roll,
No fear shall be mine, for in death as in life
He will whisper His peace to my soul.

c
It is well with my soul,
It is well, it is well with my soul.

But, Lord, for Thyself, for Thy coming we wait;
The sky, not the grave, is our goal;
O trump of the angel! O voice of the Lord!
Blessed hope! Blessed rest of my soul!

c
It is well with my soul,
It is well, it is well with my soul.


264
When the Harvest Is Past

The expression, taken from Jeremiah 8:20, "The harvest is past, the summer is ended, and we are not saved," was a lament of hopeless despair. The time of opportunity had passed.<br>Credit: "When the Harvest Is Past," S. F. Smith; C. H. F. #252

When the harvest is past and the summer is gone,
When Jesus has closed heaven's door,
When you waken at last in eternity's dawn,
When Jesus invites you no more,

c
When the harvest is past,
And the summer is gone,
Will you be with the lost,
On God's judgment be tossed,
While ages eternal roll on?

When the dreams that were cherished are dashed evermore,
No hope lights the journey ahead,
When at last souls have perished on judgment's dark shore,
All prospects of mercy have fled,

c
When the harvest is past,
And the summer is gone,
Will you be with the lost,
On God's judgment be tossed,
While ages eternal roll on?

When the ransomed have gone to their heavenly rest,
To live in those mansions above,
When their praises roll on and in choruses blest
They sing of the Savior they love,

c
When the harvest is past,
And the summer is gone,
Will you be with the lost,
On God's judgment be tossed,
While ages eternal roll on?

Can you still live at ease? Can you still feel secure,
Though hopeless - no heavenly home?
Lost where tears never cease, who could ever endure
The torments of judgment to come!

c
When the harvest is past,
And the summer is gone,
Will you be with the lost,
On God's judgment be tossed,
While ages eternal roll on?

268
O Be Saved!

The Lord Jesus said, "Come unto Me, all ye that labor and are heavy laden, and I will give you rest." Following this, a woman, whom the religious leaders called a sinner, came to Him. The Lord told her, "Thy sins are forgiven." Then He said to her, "Thy faith hath saved thee; go in peace" (Luke 7:37-50).<br>Credit: "Oh, Be Saved!" F. J. Crosby; C. H. F. #227

While God's Spirit stirs your conscience,
While the Savior still is near,
Do not hide your deep emotion,
Do not stop that falling tear.

O be saved! He waits for you;
With His wounds of love in view,
Trust Him; there's no more to do!

Jesus tenderly is waiting,
Jesus lowly, meek, and mild;
To the Friend who died to save you
Will you not be reconciled?

Do not wait until tomorrow!
You may never see its light;
Come at once! Accept His mercy!
He is waiting, come tonight!

Come, repentant, to the Savior;
Hear His call, your labors cease;
All your sins will be forgiven,
And you'll enter into peace.

All the saints and hosts in heaven
Will rejoice with Jesus' heart
When, embraced by Him who loves you,
To that home above you start.


269
While Wandering Far From the Savior

Credit: "I Was Once Far Away from the Savior," C. J. Butler; R. S. #614

While wandering far from the Savior,
Unsettled, adrift on life's sea,
I was certain that Christ, the Redeemer,
Would not care for a sinner like me.

I wandered away in the darkness,
No light or escape could I see,
And my future was clouded with sadness;
"There's no hope for a sinner like me!"

Like dawn, chasing shadows that lower,
God's Word brought the message to me
That the Savior has life-changing power,
That He loves a lost sinner like me.

How gladly I trusted in Jesus,
Who paid for my sins on the tree!
Saved by grace, I was filled with His praises,
Since He saved a lost sinner like me.

No longer in darkness I'm dwelling,
The light of His truth set me free,
And to all that I meet I am telling,
Christ has saved a lost sinner like me.

When all of life's journey is over
And I my Redeemer shall see,
I will praise Him forever and ever
That He saved a lost sinner like me.

278
We Have an Anchor

The Christian's confidence in Christ is like an anchor, because He has gone into heaven, within the veil. Hebrews 6:19 says, "Which hope we have as an anchor of the soul, both sure and stedfast, and which entereth . . . within the veil."<br>Credit: "We Have an Anchor," P. J. Owens; C. H. F. #205

Will your anchor hold in the storms of life,
When the clouds unfold fearful wings of strife?
When the storm tides lift and the cables strain,
Will your anchor drift or firm remain?

c
We have an anchor that keeps the soul
Steadfast and sure while the billows roll,
Fastened to the rock that cannot move,
Grounded firm and deep in the Savior's love.

Will your anchor hold in the straits of fear,
When the waves have told that the reef is near?
When the wild storm raves and the breakers surge,
Shall the angry waves your soul submerge?

c
We have an anchor that keeps the soul
Steadfast and sure while the billows roll,
Fastened to the rock that cannot move,
Grounded firm and deep in the Savior's love.

Will your anchor hold in the floods of death,
When the waters cold chill your final breath?
There's a hope secure that can never fail,
Anchored safe and sure "within the veil."

c
We have an anchor that keeps the soul
Steadfast and sure while the billows roll,
Fastened to the rock that cannot move,
Grounded firm and deep in the Savior's love.

Will your eyes behold on that stormy night
Heaven's street of gold and its harbor bright?
Will you anchor fast by that welcome shore,
When life's storms are past forevermore?

c
We have an anchor that keeps the soul
Steadfast and sure while the billows roll,
Fastened to the rock that cannot move,
Grounded firm and deep in the Savior's love.

285
Yet There Is Room!
Alt. Tune: "Abide with Me" (repeat last lines)
In the Parable of the Great Supper (Luke 14:16-24), the Lord Jesus described a house that was quickly filling with guests. The servant continued to invite guests because, as he said, "Yet there is room." Those words, however, were an ominous reminder that the time would come when there would be no more room.<br>Credit: "Yet There Is Room!" H. Bonar; C. H. F. #248

"Yet there is room!" The Lamb's bright hall of song
Is so inviting with its joyous throng.
Room, room, still room! Come, enter while you may!

Night chases day, the sun is sinking low,
Light is declining, and the shadows grow.
Room, room, still room! Come, enter while you may!

The bridal hall is filling for the feast;
Press in this moment; be the Bridegroom's guest.
Room, room, still room! Come, enter while you may!

Yet there is room! It is not yet too late;
The door is open, do not hesitate!
Room, room, still room! Come, enter while you may!

How soon that door may close and seal your doom!
No hope forever - now there's no more room!
No room, no room! O woeful cry, "No room!"

There's wonderful pow'r in the blood!

c
There is pow'r, pow'r, wonder-working pow'r,
In the blood of the Lamb!
There is pow'r, pow'r, wonder-working pow'r,
In the precious blood of the Lamb!

You'll find relief from your passion and pride;
There's pow'r in the blood, pow'r in the blood!
Come for a cleansing to Calvary's tide;
There's wonderful pow'r in the blood!

c
There is pow'r, pow'r, wonder-working pow'r,
In the blood of the Lamb!
There is pow'r, pow'r, wonder-working pow'r,
In the precious blood of the Lamb!

You can be cleansed and made "white as the snow";
There's pow'r in the blood, pow'r in the blood!
Sin stains are purged in its life-giving flow;
There's wonderful pow'r in the blood!

c
There is pow'r, pow'r, wonder-working pow'r,
In the blood of the Lamb!
There is pow'r, pow'r, wonder-working pow'r,
In the precious blood of the Lamb!

You can have peace with the heavenly King;
There's pow'r in the blood, pow'r in the blood!
Then you'll live daily His praises to sing;
There's wonderful pow'r in the blood!

c
There is pow'r, pow'r, wonder-working pow'r,
In the blood of the Lamb!
There is pow'r, pow'r, wonder-working pow'r,
In the precious blood of the Lamb!


287
Jesus Is a Rock In the Time of Storm
Tune: "Weary Land"
The Old Testament often refers to the Lord as a Rock. David said, "Lead me to the rock that is higher than I. For Thou hast been a shelter for me" (Psalm 61:2, 3). The prophet adds, "A Man shall be as an hiding place from the wind . . . as the shadow of a great rock in a weary land" (Isaiah 32:2).<br>Credit: "A Sinner Bound for Eternity"; G. H. B. #2

Your soul must face eternity;
Find shelter for the time of storm.
The Savior says, "Come unto Me";
He shelters from the coming storm!

c
Yes, Jesus is a Rock in the time of storm,
The time of storm, the time of storm.
Yes, Jesus is a Rock in the raging storm;
He shelters from the wrath to come.

He suffered wrath at Calvary;
There's shelter for the time of storm.
He died and rose; now He can be
Your shelter from the coming storm.

c
Yes, Jesus is a Rock in the time of storm,
The time of storm, the time of storm.
Yes, Jesus is a Rock in the raging storm;
He shelters from the wrath to come.

The clouds are dark; how can you sleep
Not sheltered for the time of storm?
Awake or you'll forever weep,
Not sheltered in the coming storm!

c
Yes, Jesus is a Rock in the time of storm,
The time of storm, the time of storm.
Yes, Jesus is a Rock in the raging storm;
He shelters from the wrath to come.

The storm will break with awesome might;
There's shelter for the time of storm.
That storm will rage through endless night;
Take shelter from the coming storm!

c
Yes, Jesus is a Rock in the time of storm,
The time of storm, the time of storm.
Yes, Jesus is a Rock in the raging storm;
He shelters from the wrath to come.


288
You're Not Very Far
Tune: "Haven of Rest"
Among His questioners, the Lord Jesus singled out a sincere student of the Law. The Lord said to him, "Thou art not far from the kingdom of God" (Mark 12:34).<br>Credit: "Thou Art Not Very Far"; G. H. B. #254

You're not very far from the kingdom of God;
You're hearing the call of the King,
Who sent forth His servants to travel abroad,
His welcoming offer to bring.
Their message appeals, but the world seems so dear,
With glamour and pleasure and sin;
How sad it would be to see heaven so near,
Yet never to enter therein!

c
Yes, not very far from salvation by grace;
Be warned of your danger! Beware!
For "not very far" is a perilous place;
You'll perish by lingering there.

You're not very far from the foot of the cross,
So near to that life-giving tree,
Where grace that will rescue the sinner from loss
Invites you to come and be free.
That cross of redemption, love's measureless sea!
That saving or sentencing sight!
How tragic to stand near the foot of that tree,
Yet never be cleansed and made right!

c
Yes, not very far from salvation by grace;
Be warned of your danger! Beware!
For "not very far" is a perilous place;
You'll perish by lingering there.

How many once stood by that heavenly door,
But trifled their moment away!
Now hopelessly weeping, they're lost evermore;
Hell's darkness has banished their day.
They're far from the kingdom and far from the crown,
From Christ and His ransoming cross.
O infinite sadness! No tears but His own
Can weep such a fathomless loss.

c
Yes, not very far from salvation by grace;
Be warned of your danger! Beware!
For "not very far" is a perilous place;
You'll perish by lingering there.


289
Around the Grave of Jesus
Tune: "Greenland's Icy Mountains" (Missionary)
Credit: "Around Thy Grave, Lord Jesus," J. G. Deck; C. H. F. #525

Around the grave of Jesus,
His empty grave, we stand,
With gratitude and praises,
To keep the Lord's command,
By faith, our souls rejoicing,
To trace His path of love
Through death's dark, angry billows,
Up to the throne above.

With worship, we remember
His anguish on the tree,
The waves of wrath engulfing
The Lamb on Calvary,
Baptized in death's cold waters.
For us His blood was shed;
For us, the Lord of Glory,
Was numbered with the dead.

The Victor, He is risen;
Our doubts and fears are gone;
For sin He once has suffered;
He lives on heaven's throne.
Sin, death, and hell are vanquished
By Him, the Church's Head,
And now we share His triumphs,
The Firstborn from the dead.

We're baptized in these waters
Because with Him we died;
With Him, our Life, we're risen
And in Him glorified;
From sin, the world, and Satan,
We're ransomed by His blood.
All glory and dominion
To Christ, the Lamb of God!


290
Buried in the Grave of Jesus
Tune: "Rise, My Soul! Behold 'Tis Jesus" (Gotha)
Credit: "Buried in the Grave of Jesus," Mrs. J. A. Trench; C. H. F. #526

Buried in the grave of Jesus,
We believe what God has said;
Faith, His judgment acquiescing,
Reckons now that we are dead.

Death and judgment are behind us;
Grace and glory are ahead.
All the waves rolled over Jesus;
We have peace and calm instead.

Firstfruit of the resurrection,
He is risen from the tomb;
Now we stand in new creation,
Free, delivered from our doom.

Jesus died and we died with Him,
Buried in His grave to lie,
One with Christ in resurrection,
Seated now in Him on high.

We await the full redemption,
When the risen One shall come,
And our resurrected bodies
Shall be fashioned like His own.

Lord, we share in Thy rejection;
Thy reproach, O may we love;
Here we stand in Thine acceptance
In the Father's sight above.


291
Buried in Symbol
Tune: Hursley
Credit: "Buried in Symbol"; C. H. F. #527

Is it Thy will that I should be
Buried in symbol, Lord, with Thee?
To all the world, this solemn sign
Declares the truth that I am Thine.

Gladly I'd be submissive now;
In all things to Thy will I'd bow;
My joy is to obey Thy Word,
Follow Thy steps, my sovereign Lord.

This chosen symbol of Thy grave
Shows forth Thy love, so strong and brave;
Buried with Thee, I now proclaim
My heart's devotion to Thy name.

Out of the grave, O Lord, I come,
For Thou art risen from the tomb;
Thy resurrection life I share,
Thy Lordship in my life declare.

By grace, I count myself to be
Dead to the sins that wounded Thee;
Alive to God, I worship, serve,
And yield to Thee without reserve.

Lord Jesus, when I gaze on Thee
And all Thy shining glory see,
That joy will far exceed the shame
I bear on earth for Thy loved name.
